O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, my very dear children, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science, its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is closely guarded in our region and unknown everywhere, the knowledge has decayed and been lost, and there remains no stronger evidence than the small descriptions in old books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this, error and vanity have arisen, and thoughts are closed, and knowledge is separated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive this treatise by organizing it according to the order of exposure and explanation and abbreviation; I will bring together the forms of cauterizing tools and other instruments used in the work with adjustments to the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes to master this science of anatomy, as Galen says, that he know the judgment of the members, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and blood vessels, and the number of them, and the movement and resting of veins and arteries, and from where they come.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that the name without action is meaningless, and the work alone is good; especially in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the beginning of this book that he who is not acquainted with the things aforementioned, risks error and mistaking people; as I have often seen many of those who undertake this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a most terrible sight, where a scrofula (scrofulous swelling) had formed on the neck of a woman, and it was eating into her arteries; so much blood issued forth that the woman died in the woman's hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another sight where a stone was removed from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; it tore out a piece of his bladder, and he bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; I knew well that if they attempted to remove it, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another wonder that took in charge the Duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture he had a wound; the doctors, full of ignorance, bound the fracture to the wound as if by strong ropes, leaving no space for healing, and left it thus until the end; and commanded him not to unbind it; and he waited until the leg was completely swelled and painful, and it came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	They called me to come to him, and I hurried to unbind the leg; and when I loosened it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corrupting it was already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I also saw another wonder that the abscess, which had been healed, suddenly became inflamed due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is free from black bile, it does not need to be cut with iron unless it is in a part that can be entirely removed without leaving any corrupted tissue.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear child, it is necessary for you to know that the art of healing is divided into two parts: that is, work involving danger in various ways; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, guard yourself so that the foolish eye cannot speak ill of you; take up your weapons courageously and attack your illnesses lightly but firmly, using the best method so that through the grace of God you may be saved and be happy; cast away diseases filled with despair and give up nothing to doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his warnings: "Do not take any illness seriously, unless you are called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and medicinal agues, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the tools for cauterization, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it includes the ordering and forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; it orders the use of the most important instruments, and the shapes of tools.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, as we remember the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of the aid and the harm or benefit of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and their harmful or beneficial effects are the longest speech and subtlest science, containing secret answers; about these things, the most wise have spoken, and they agree on them; and their words suffice me little, as I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for every complexion where it has matter, whether the complexions: that is to say, a hot complexion with material, and a dry complexion without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion, matter combines, and they devised no remedy but said that cautery is great help; and the others said the opposite: that cautery is of no avail for ailments arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated for hot ailments with heat or dryness, but rather with cold; and he who says otherwise claims that cautery provides great help to hot and dry ailments that come upon the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the color of fire, you perceive the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should attempt it except he who has tried it and knows through long practice the chapter of cautery, and the variety of human complexes, and their dispositions and causes of illness, and the remedies and the times of day; for other complexes we have only fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and consented to the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, child, that cauterization combines fire in a way that is part of healing secrets and, moreover, offers greater gentleness than medicinal burning.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from outside unless it affects a hot member, and it does not harm any other member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines that burn come from one member to another by spreading, and bring diseases of grief rather than healing; and sometimes the fire causes the patient pain due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance if there is too much of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And if you have found me through experience and the long service and study that I have devoted to this art, and it is in accordance with the truth of things; and because I excuse myself for the length of my speech, as I do not like to deprive you of the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from bodies, as the philosopher says by demonstrating; then accept it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agree on the time when cauterization must be performed, and carefully select the instruments.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the pain-relieving effect of the procedure removes the source of harm; and especially when cauterization is required to alleviate severe pain or a pressing condition that cannot wait for a more suitable time.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do who follow folly; for a disease that is healed by cautery has no relapse; and thus it should be. But it is not like they care for it, because cautery is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries up humors which are the cause of pain, and acts more swiftly than other medicines through the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another powerful thing is that the disease comes according to the state of the patient and the nature of the illness, and excesses accumulate within it through the acquisition of foods and similar things; except for cautery applied where there are few excesses or moisture, as in cauterization for pain and similar conditions, then this pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand at all why cautery is called the last of medicine, but it is true; yet they do not believe that cautery has value after medicine, for when we administer methods of treatment for any illness and they are useless, then we use cautery, and it is beneficial.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last of medicine, not at all according to the opinion of wise men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with gold instruments is more effective than with iron, and they did not consider fire to be harsh because of the quality of gold or the excellence of its substance; they said that the heat of cauterization does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true, as I have tested it and found that it is indeed harmful to no one; cautery with gold is more effective than with iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat the gold instrument, you are not certain if it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and as soon as it has cooled down; and if you heat it too much, it becomes spoiled; thus there is ample hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use the fire cautery that we have equipped for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now therefore I have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the path may be easier to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery should be applied to the head with moisture and cold, and there are many ailments caused by this method, known as "soda", due to the descent of humors from the head to the limbs and ears, and also due to dreams, toothaches, throat pain, and particularly, diseases arising from coldness, such as paralysis, soda (a term likely referring to a type of stroke), apoplexy, and similar ailments.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a solvent medicine that cleanses the head, either three times or four times, according to the virtue and age and habit of the patient, and then the head should be re-heated.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make it rest crossed in your hands, and place his hands on some weight; afterward, put the root of your palm onto the root of its neck between its two joints; and leave it where your two middle fingers will be, if it bleeds, then heat the cautery called 'olive' which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mark it on the skin with ink, then gently lower and stretch your hand, causing some tremor; then lift your hand slowly, and examine the bone if you see it is intact; and if not, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. Afterward, take a small amount of silk, put soft butter and cotton inside, place it on the skin, and leave it for three days; then apply more cotton soaked in butter; and continue until the burning from the cautery is gone; finally, treat the wound with the remedy called 'tetrafarmacon' as long as it remains clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say that the older a wound is, the more it purifies itself; and for this reason, one must help it along.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one should not let the fire cautery burn off any part of the bone, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another says that one should let the cautery burn so deeply, and push it with such force that bone is removed as wide as a woman's ring finger, so that humors can flow out; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; afterward, one should clean and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every way, except for people who have no fear; and I believe I should leave them; for the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness it in other members; and even when the patient's joint is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization seems safer and more mobile to me, and from this, I proceed accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes and lasts for a long time, patients should use herbs and pills known as "cough drops," as well as gargles and compresses; and if one performs the cauterization we have mentioned above, it is of no avail.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature and not too rigid; then cauterize it from below, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each horn of the shoulder up to the bone, as we have said before, and cauterize the one called "vasselz," which is where the suction cups are placed; hold your hand slightly away so that you do not see the bone. The patient feels much greater pain from this cauterization than from others, which I will speak of later; it is important that the cauterization of the horns be more precise than that of the middle part of the shoulder, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head there is sudden pain, and the disease extends to the oil (or possibly referring to inflammation or swelling), and the condition is purged with medicated remedies, and all other cures as I have mentioned in the division of diseases, but none of these help: then perform cauterization according to two methods, that is, with ague medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with ague medicine is when you apply a hot compress to the affected area, remove the skin and scrape the raw flesh gently, then make an incision in the same manner that the pain is felt, so that you can lift the affected part of the head from below the skin; and when it is lifted, tightly bind it and leave it for 12 hours. Then unbind it and treat the wound firmly, leaving it uncovered for 2-3 days, then apply a cotton plug soaked in butter until the swelling subsides.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment as long as it is healed; and if you see that something similar to any of the burning medicines I have written about or dosed in treating burning medicines occurs, then...
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this tool:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a closed space where a little heat can be contained; and then place it on the painful limb, hold your hand, and turn it slightly so that half of the thickness of the heart is burned; and then remove your hand so the artery does not burn, which is dangerous, and abundant blood flows.

After placing cotton in awe of silk, and laying it on the wound for three days; then he moistens it with butter, and continues to treat the wound with medicine until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare' (a sharp instrument), be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When treating migraine as we have previously described in the sections about diseases, and it does not benefit from the cautery that is usually applied and its effect is insufficient, then you must reheat the cautery called 'cultellare' until it becomes white; then press on the wound that needs treatment with a line of half a finger's length, withdraw your hand once, making sure not to damage the artery so as not to cause bone fractures; guard against the jaw muting when chewing, and the teeth should only focus on muting, preventing spasms from affecting the patient, and beware of blood loss from the artery after it has been cut, especially for those who are inexperienced, and be careful with decomposition of blood in the artery, or its severing will cause great fear, especially to those who do not know how to handle it; leave the treatment halfway done. But I will tell you how to prevent blood loss when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it heals in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice against the disease, and the patient suffers, cauterize the affected area on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is clean; and if you notice, apply the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery, along with a cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful.

de la torture de la bouche	regarding the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture that requires cautery is limited to those that involve fluid movement, as we have mentioned in the divisions of illness; and do not perform cautery on parts that exhibit dryness, inflammation, and pain.

Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the appearance of cutting that we have described above, but it is a little more subtle, and it is necessary that the knife be a little thicker; after that, treat it as I have said before, while it is healthy.

de litargie	It seems like there might be a slight error or missing context

de la froidor dou chief	from the coldness of the head

de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy

Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you need to cauterize, make several incisions throughout the entire cautery.

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Let the body shed tears from its eyes.

dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that does not allow the oil to pass through

For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

After cauterizing the affected area little by little several times, burn the nearby nerves; and the sign of the work's success is that you see the skin retracting and the hairs standing on end at the touch of oil; then lift your hand and leave it for three days, after which apply moistened cotton in butter until the burning sensation disappears; subsequently, treat the wound as long as it remains healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil. Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical cautery with burning drugs, you should instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment shape of the leaf of mirta. Take French soap and bright charcoal, each in equal amounts, grind them together thoroughly; apply it gently so as not to chill, then spread it over the shape made like the leaf of mirta, and place paper over it. If the illness persists in one oil only, one should operate in both, and if in both, pour cotton oil moistened with egg white under it. The patient's part should be in your healthy hand, and show it to the medicine; press a little and move it back and forth whenever the patient feels the sting of the medicine, for he will feel the sting just as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the infection has passed, then raise the limb slowly, and observe if you see the skin raised as it was before by constraint of fire or incision; and if so, it is good.

If not, apply more medicine to the limb, but ensure the treatment is not excessive, keeping your work even and precise; then cover it with moistened butter cloth until the pain is alleviated, after which cure the limb with the dressing known as 'dyafenis' and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you, guard yourself well with your work, taking great care that it does not neglect the medicine at all.

Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the needs of men are diverse in size and extent, and according to those constraints; and do not turn away from the right path to him who has the knowledge of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have explained in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you should cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head on a healthy surface; then take their hand and position it between your hands in such a way that their head does not move or wiggle; afterward, apply moist cotton soaked in wine or persil juice over the area; subsequently, heat up the cauterizing iron until it is hot. Position the cautery at the base of the head, shaping it like a feather, so that it touches both sides; if you see it pointed downwards towards one side, or upwards as well, or if it resembles a tent, but regardless of its shape, this is acceptable for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it and drain the pus and moisture; if it is closed, cut it open and draw out the bowels; then apply hot cautery, holding your hand over the cauterized area above the oil, so that your hand does not cause harm; and place the cautery on the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery near the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not work, repeat the cautery again, and if you need to, do it a third time, leaving it for three days; then apply moistened cotton in butter, and cure the wound from the drying agent as long as it is clean, and if forty days pass and it is not clean, apply hot corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow this according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that no one from the past spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula and fix its location; then place a subtle heat source into the gap, thus taking on this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it makes the quantity of a drop of water; and hold your hand firmly as the heat source, so that the patient does not move at all, so that the drop does not leave its place, and it is good to put moist cotton on the patient in order to achieve effect or healing: the drop adheres strongly to the fistula, and health returns through miraculous sanity.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by cautery as we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this does not happen, then it is necessary to administer warmth or cold, and bring the fistula back to the body according to what is appropriate for its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips

de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat

When an abscess forms in the root of the throat, or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, leading to putrefaction, gangrene, and becoming a fistula, then treat it as we have said in detail, but it does not benefit; then you must apply cautery according to the size of the fistula; after opening or removing the fistula, hold your hand until the heat from the fire reaches the bottom, and leave it there; and do this once or twice after treating it as we have said in detail, until it is healed; and if it heals thus, that is good; but if not, you must expose the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find described in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers. Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the teeth that were moving will be confirmed, and the softened gums restrained, and the moisture corrupted dried up.
de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of teeth comes from coldness, whether there is a chill or frost, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cautery according to two methods: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	The butter cautery is such that you press melted butter into a brass or iron spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a stick, moisten it in the melted butter, and apply it to the aching tooth gently, holding it until it cools; do this frequently until its effect reaches the root of the tooth. If you see that the moisture from the cloth and cotton has been absorbed by the butter, and you apply it to the aching tooth, then place a hot iron on top while the heat penetrates the tooth's surface.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He uses fire cautery if it is such that you press a piece of iron or silver into the patient's wound, and it is so thick that the heat does not reach the mouth of the wound; after heating the cautery, from which the shape will come as we shall see later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be lessened on that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then apply heat; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on the part of the body where you wish, according to your ability; and this is the shape of the instrument.
des scrophules	Of scrofula (a form of tuberculosis affecting the

Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two incisions around the bones; and if there is no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize every part, and do good governance to the patient and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you govern it well and drain the moisture, it will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	De la routure dou syfac" translates directly to "Of the dislocation of
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When dislocation occurs in the arm, and the joints descend to the elbows, it is new, so it is important that when you see this, you do not move him immediately; and use things that leave the belly, so that the intestines fall from his belly. After making him lie on his back between your hands, command him to hold his breath until the joints are repaired, and straighten them at your will, and sign across the break in the bone of the wrist, and make a mark like half a circle above the body; then take the fire cautery whose form is as described here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it sheds scales.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their proper place; and the minister should place his hand so that they do not return backward; and open well the thighs of the patient, and put under him pillows and supports on the thighs, and another one on the buttocks which hold his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and firm until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, repeat it again until you come to the bone; and be careful that the joint does not pop when you perform the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is useless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery of children be delicate according to their size, and of adults also large according to their measure; after three days, treat the wound with butter until the scald is healed; afterwards, cure other wounds until they are sane, and lay the patient on his back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that his movements be restricted for a long time, so that the boils do not appear when he goes to his rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, a well-made bandage is applied to him and left for another forty days; and he should have good rest, working little and guarding against excessive drinking and eating, and from loud shouting; and with this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment for cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known not to grow larger, the treatment involves cauterization with a hot iron according to its quantity, starting from the third day; after this, follow the cure as we have described; and no elder has said that it should be cauterized with a three-pointed iron in this manner.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the skin with a sharp instrument and make a line across the width above the dislocation, and another one further away, and hold your hand firmly over the entire cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the initial cauterization is lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any member, either from weakness or an injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medicine provides no relief, then it is necessary to cauterize the affected area with a instrument called "poins," and the cauterization should be done according to the length of the member, its smallness or largeness, its strength or weakness, its position, and the nature of the pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healthy after the first cautery, that's good; otherwise, start again with a new cautery on the same area, as it often happens that he should move in the limb next to where the cautery was performed, so you should do cauterizations until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	It seems like there might have been a slight error or missing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	These diseases are never helped by a single cautery, especially the illness that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can cauterize it, taking care if the disease is in its beginning and if it is curable according to what we have said before, and do not delay or hesitate, and doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the patient; then perform two cauterizations on the head: one new on the top of the head, and the other towards the front at the end of the hair; on both temples, and behind on the nape; leaving your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is proper.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is widespread and clearly evident, it is necessary that you cauterize these cauterizations that we have mentioned above, and cauterize them in some places, and make six cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one great one on the croup and another on a delicate place, and two on each shoulder; and two on the elbows, and two on the tender parts of the pis, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the pits of the hands; and beware of the nails that are on the last toe, so you do not burn them. Never make a cauterization on the bone of the wrist, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cautery, the greater the aid it brings and the better it works; and know that the sick do not feel pain from cautery as the healthy do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be great or small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the manner of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply a poultice of meal with honey and other remedies until it is cleansed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but it remains inflamed, then make cautery on the member according to its size and the extent of the swelling; and let the cautery be a little deep into the heart of the pain; then apply treatments with oil until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the point of a nerve that controls the limb, and thus is removed the swelling; nevertheless, no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the passage of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of alba (or white)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is ignited, and the medical science has no effect, then cauterize it slightly with a hot iron according to the severity of the case, until the white is removed, and the color changes; then apply a cure made of flour, beans, and plantain leaves, with rose oil and alder sap, each separately, and mix them all together, wrap it in cloth, and keep it at the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of the ulcer (chancre) by cauterization.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a ulcer (chancre) appears in its initial stages, and you wish to stop its progression, cauterize it with an iron that forms a circle around the entire ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise say that one should also perform cauterization in the midst of a chancre; nevertheless, I do not find this good, for I fear it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen many times; and a more just thing is that it be cauterized around, in the cauterization called 'circular', as we have said regarding many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called 'adubelati', and they do not want to die, either because of the excessive fluid it produces or due to the age of the patient when they are weak (that is, too much), and there is little blood, or because of time; and you see them hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauterizations by piercing; after that, leave it alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through entirely with the cautery, the heat of which is as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the midst of this ill-named 'adubelati' (disease) while the cautery has pierced through, making it like the cautery so that the patient feels no further pain in such a way that the course of the rotting is halted.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure, until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens," which is nothing other than a weakening of the limbs, as it affects the members just as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a limb that can be treated with fire cautery, then warm the cautery claws both small and large, according to what is suitable for the limb or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you reach all the corruption, leave nothing of it, so that everything that is corrupt is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and place on the joints cauterized, suffering from burning with oil until all the scorches from the fire are healed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that cause pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that the pain does not subside, it is good; and if not, repeat the cauterization on the joint that has remained corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture is sometimes treated with a medicinal remedy instead of fire cauterization; but nevertheless, fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already described the treatment with medicinal remedies in detail: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from the pieces which come as fragments
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that pieces due to deficiencies arise a disease called "close" according to our intention, and it is a great wrong that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	For the fire cautery, take a hot knife that is sharp like a quill and made of good iron, so it can pierce the nail from all sides, and have it with subtle edges; then place it hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it goes to the bottom of the nail; leave it thus for three days until it begins to corrupt; then make a poultice of wild mallows crushed with silk, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will split and be pulled out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound with fresh, clean bandages until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are moved by heat, the body's strength is often broken and it happens in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and this is how: take a cane of iron or steel, or a pen of voutel, and place the nail and the glue, that is to say pitch, on warts; and put the cane around it so that it surrounds everything, then add a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning it until the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and you can find the hot water path all the way to the root; and allow the patient to bear the stinging of hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will come out at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, make one after another, as you stretch all those that are in the body, then cure the wounds that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	it cures the shaking of the body.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone trembles from cold or quartan fever or any other (condition), it is necessary that you perform four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the feet, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; if this stops the trembling, and hastens the healing from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is it apparent through external defects or pus-filled blisters that come from deeply corrupted, putrid matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary to act immediately when they appear, applying cautery to each pustule: a delicate cautery of fir wood, with which the point is taken to fire, or of long root of aristo loge, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should cauterization be performed at the outset when they appear, according to this manner, for it cannot grow worse in progress, but is broken off the excess from which it comes, and becomes healthy; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many serious consequences often arise from the blood of an artery that is cut in a wound, or at the end of a vein, or during cauterization of a member, and similar cases; it is a very sorrowful thing to be smelly.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	However, if it happens to anyone, be quick to place your finger on the wound of the vein, and pull very strongly until the pain is completely gone from under your thumb; then take several small and large olive oil cauterization tools while they are entirely red hot; then, according to the size or smaller of the wound, insert them and hold the cautery against the vein where you are holding your finger, and keep it there until the pain subsides.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden spark flies when you cut your vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to apply one after the other until the wound is healed; be careful not to burn the nerve that lies beneath, and let no further harm come to the patient; and know that when the flow from the artery has ceased, it cannot be adequately stopped again, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cauterization, or extraction when it is not treated, or tightly binding it with strong thread, or applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and it should be bound and restrained carefully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers relief from a tight ligature by placing rags or burning items on it, or similar things, will not benefit unless he does so carefully.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he has no suitable medicine at hand, then he should apply his finger to the wound of the vein as we have said, pressing hard until all pain disappears from the wound and the vein; and he must not move it, but moisten it with cold water frequently, so long as it is very cold, frozen, swollen, and painful; and prepare cauterization tools and medicines as needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we have explained the applications, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterization; I have placed this chapter after the one on the head because it is easier for those who wish to learn.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before we begin, it is necessary for you to know that this chapter involves greater risk and fear than the first one on cauterization; therefore, more caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to attempt folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come to healing.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who are so possessed by their illness that they die lightly because of the severity of the disease they suffer and the greatness of their suffering; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who lose their senses, saying: "Wait, I am blind"; and the illness is terrifying.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place greater emphasis on your honor than on their greed; do not act rashly, but prudently regarding what is certain and what can be acquired safely; and use divination and indication in treating your patients, so that health may be restored; for this will help you gain a good reputation, glory, and lasting fame.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most noble son, our lords grant you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered this chapter for you, in considering by chapters, according to what is before or in the chapter of cautery, which I have devised from the head down to the feet, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	chief filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the child's head is too tightly squeezed, it results in no response as there is no time to act.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and it hastens the death of all those that I have seen; and for this reason, I think it is better to leave part of the treatment unfinished.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw children whose joints were filled with water, and the head became swollen each day until it could not be supported; and because of the moisture, they believed that they would die, and this moisture was so concentrated beneath the skin on the bone in the armpit between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is such that you make a wide cut through the head where the moisture is located; it should be as long as we mentioned, as long as the moisture flows; and see here the shape of the spatula.
