Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the openings of the commissures widely gaping in each part, and there is a sharp, strong flow when you press with your hand from within, and it does not return, then you must make three cuts in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the cracks in cloths and powders, and applying wine and oil, leave it thus for up to five days; then release it, and treat the wound with bandages and plasters, and stretch the head equally, and give the patient dry meat from a bag of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is to observe or open the size of the abscess, and the arrangement of the fluid; for it never appears in front; nor behind; nor on the right; nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the abscess open, and drain the fluid, and make the cut according to your ability; be careful not to block the artery; and if blood flows, it will cause the patient to die slowly from bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of the flame cautery, instruct the patient to
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone suffers from a disease called "cataract" in one or both eyes, and the illness is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the final remedy is the cautery with which they will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when the patient opens their eyes, to make them close; then rub the affected area with a rough cloth until the arteries open, and pull the cloth firmly from the wound; then examine where the vein flows, and the veins on both sides should be located behind the ears, completely closed; then mark the veins with a signet, and cut both of them with a sharp spatula, reaching down to the bone, making an incision as wide as possible through the forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, turn the spatula beneath the artery and cut through the tissue above, cutting just as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously unless held above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pressed, you must measure the amount of space of three fingers, then tie it with twine and make it stop bleeding; and this is six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if it remains on the bone without pus, do not remove the clot that has formed at the base, but stretch and bind the wound, and treat it with care until it heals.
de emigrainne	from migraine pain
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine pain occurs, accompanied by catarrh due to moisture in the eyes and cheeks, and the persistent and similar symptoms of old age, it is treated with various medical cures, but often none of them help; then we must drain the arteries in the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from his temples and locates the artery which opens in the temple, as it opens clearly due to its pulsation, and it is quickly sealed off unless in very delicate people; if it is sealed off, the patient gently pulls on some cloth, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and soaks it with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula with this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it with pincers and separate the threads that attach it to each part; if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the number of joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will never stop causing pain entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the abscess with six incisions, as far as three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it with two strands of strong silk thread so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound and causes further problems; then cut off the excess between the two threads at the same time, and if you see fit, cauterize the wound with a cutting instrument until the joints are cut through; this is the moving part, if the patient does not have fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is aid to finish moisture: therefore it is of greater aid for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with cotton wool and cover it with well-made bandages; and when they are removed, apply dried medicines that produce heat, and bandages until it heals; and if you do not have these at hand, soak a cloth in vitriole (a corrosive substance) and apply pressure on the artery until it is sterilized; and if you don't have this, put ice on the wound until the artery is congealed, and then remove the ice with cold water as needed, and tighten it properly. The warmer and lighter method for extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with a sharp instrument from both sides, but the cuts should be well-spaced to prolong their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instruments are too tight, they hold the heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two blades a space as thick as a finger, and then when you have marked the two joints with the pen, and place the hot iron over until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two joints; and they should be separated between the two joints because this cautery is not properly sealed throughout; and this is the shape of the cauterization.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes descend into the veins that are on the head and face, and no medicine helps, you see the face of the patient contort, and feel their forehead moving as if from a fever, and the eyes are red and moist so that the paper-like skin falls off, and the skin is scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this ancient cure "contused cure", and for the patient suffering from this condition, you should let the hairs on their forehead grow, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly according to its length; one cut should go all the way down to the nose, and the other two should be at an angle on either side of the forehead, not touching the arteries that are beside the papers. Keep your hand away from the joint of the lower jaw, making each wound about three fingers wide across. And have a piece of sponge and cloth ready to wipe the blood, then use the pointed instrument as shown:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the heart that is between the two fissures to all the satisfaction that is on the bone, then make another from the middle incision up to the other second, and then extract this spatule.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultele" into the first fissure, and it is very sharp on one side and soft on the other, this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the cutting side towards the opposite edge at the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the last one until the incision is continuous to open the heart, and then make another narrow incision to the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the flesh for the blood taken; then put in each wound a strip of old cotton, and cover with moistened cloths in wine and oil and flax, and be sure that no abscesses form; on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer a strong injection of cold water, then apply basilicon treatment with rose oil, and other remedies to cure wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	your head
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	For when any catarrh has become accustomed to the veins, you see them swollen and small, weakening vision, burning papers; the hair falls out, and it feels painful to touch, causing the patient to sneeze; then know by these symptoms that this matter and catarrh do not come from a single vein, but rather multiple ones, and the movement of the cure is what it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to bend their forehead backward, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another one quite wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And starting from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, make an incision reaching the bone; move your hand away from the nerve of the temples that move with blinking; and when the bone is exposed, rinse all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the cut and place old cotton in it, and cover it with linen. Then, put moistened cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and keep it warm to prevent infection. When the bone is removed, rub the bone gently until it starts to heal, then apply drying agents that help healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower and three parts of colophony, mix them to make a paste, and apply it to these wounds to soothe them throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear inflammation
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes pain in the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, mineral stones, or similar objects; seeds, such as peas, beans, and other legumes; or fluid-like substances like water and air.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When anything, whether it's a stone or another object that does not fit properly in the ear, causes pain or does not grow inside the ear, place the affected ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, and it distills any little bit of purple oil or sesamum oil, then it is ready for extraction; and it causes a sneezing from the condition, and stops the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and puts pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and lets the ear open up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often times, this treatment brings about fever; and if it does not bring fever, then extraction with delicate pincers is performed, like so:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the pincers, that's good; if not, perform extraction with an extremely fine needle of small gauge; and if it still does not jump out, make a chain of iron and press the chain or something similar firmly on the head of the stone in the ear canal, so that the coming air cannot enter with the stone; then treat it thoroughly, because often times fever results as we have said; and if it does not result in this way, take much care in choosing the instrument, and place some cotton inside; then press the iron on the stone (or whatever) and extract it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not depart from all these things that we have said, then quickly pierce the ear in the same manner as an abscess forms and hardens, and the spasm; and the method of the incision is such that you first heal the patient suffering from a cephalalgia, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and return the ear to its original position, making a small incision at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue hangs down; and let the incision be as thin as a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your skill, and suck it into your mouth; and the cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains that are stuck together and swollen, then perform extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then administer a delicate spatula according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make sure to perform a careful incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not rush to conclude that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, unless you have made many attempts; then extract it with subtle pincers and suck gently, as we have said, so that extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case where you extract something from the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use a strong sneeze immediately afterward and open the ear with cotton wool.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lay something on that same ear, whether there is moisture or not.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps through fire, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If the fire is no longer hot, take many small reeds according to the length of your thumb and forefinger, and warm them slightly over the fire; then put them into the patient's ear, and try from another side, and insert another reed onto the reed inside the ear; and do this with one reed upon another until the water is completely gone, and thus it will jump out completely; and if you see, take a thin thread, and pull one of the reeds inside the ear, and the other with fire as long as the thinner reed burns; then make more reeds in the same way until all the water is gone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the removal of an animal, if it is small like a flea or something similar, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large, one must use pliers for its extraction, and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When dealing with worms in the ears, after treating it as we have mentioned in the previous section and while managing the distillations, if the cure does not work, you should examine the ear under sunlight. If there are no visible worms, use fine pliers to remove them, and if they still cannot be seen, take a look at the shape of the canal.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tight from below and wide from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then apply the most subtle suction in the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suck repeatedly throughout the entire chain; do this often until all the pain disappears.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then close the chain with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tried in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using all these instruments, which is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a piece of silver or gold thread cut into small pieces, and over them pour water to distill; and using a well-made brass instrument, press the distillation down, taking a razor and wrapping it tightly around the tip with cotton; then pour in your oil or juice, and whatever you wish from your medicine in the vessel, and let the vessel be in the ear. Then put the razor back into all the cotton and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or the liquid has left the ear; and let the patient smell it, and be sure that the distillation is not too hot, for the medicine would not then be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear inflammation
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with any perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a wound or some object stuck inside the ear, and this obstruction comes completely closed up in the ear if one cannot see it; and never does the perforation become wider, and one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When it becomes completely blocked if one cannot see it, it is due to poor healing in various ways, and in this case, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the swelling prominent, then there is a form of all these spines here.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make incisions and cuts on both the front and back, so that it does not injure the ear; if the inflammation is from a foreign body or the cartilage of the ear, with delicate pincers, hold it slightly, until all the bone is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the inflammations are completely in the ear, take a fine, sharp razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then insert it into the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation in the ear that the patient experiences as sharp, make a slight perforation and be careful not to damage the eardrum; then insert into the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Apply no pressure until the wound is healed, or take a cloth and moisten it in rosewater, and sprinkle vitriol powder on it; and if you notice an ear swelling, it is necessary to remove the cloth and apply another moistened cloth made of rosin oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it as long as it is clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other remedies to remove the bleeding which are treated through distillation.
de la char des papieres	on the subject of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Gather all the papers that come from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to extend them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off the top of a spatula from its roots; then put it on the vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after removing the outer layer, the cautery is performed with a delicate lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incision moves; and often they repair themselves, as no part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of frost
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come upon paper certain things that seem greasy in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "frost," and it is a gathering of much moisture on the paper from above and below; the work is thus: be wary if the frost becomes silent on one side and the other, which is a light thing to know; then make them wide apart, and scrape gently from each part, then take hold of them with pincers and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the split is large, and the gathering has a stitch, then treat it while it is still healthy; but if it is small, make no great effort, for the humors will soon restore it and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pain is descending within the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper against it, and the pain will grasp with a squeeze, and the beating on both sides; and if the paper is removed by incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut off, drain the water and heal the affected area until the patient is cured.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is contained within the tissues of the paper-like skin over the eyes, and it occurs more often in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes. It leads to cataracts in the morning, preventing them from looking at the light of the sun because tears constantly flow from their eyes. Due to this, they lie down on their faces and sleep, with their paper-like skin under their eyebrows moistened by the exinach, which has formed within their eyes.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the pain between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient places his head in a healthy position; then he takes a linen cloth and prepares a tent-like shape according to the quantity of blood from each part, placing it on top; and presses with his fingers on both sides so that the blood is collected within the circular shape; then, using a sharp spatula, they make a cut as wide as the wound made in the vein, but no larger; and they continue to make the incision until they reach the blood; and in various positions, blood comes out from the cut in the form of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then a whole piece of cloth between your fingers over the wound, and move your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to press into the gap, do not reach all the way to the oil, or blow on it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the gap does not open at first, gently widen the gap as much as it opens; then take it out as we have said, and moisten cloth with water and salt, and place it on the wound, and bind tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who grind and apply something to corrupt the moisture that is lingering.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him as long as he is sane.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the hot abscess, treat it with external applications as long as he is sane.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in papers (abnormally), they become tangled, causing harm as if they were like tears, and lead to soft or hardened papers, and albugine (a type of skin condition), due to the destruction of the hair; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cauterization with fire, or by using a medicine that corresponds to this chapter on cautery, or by incision and stitching, or by binding, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's affected head in your healthy hand, then turn the paper from the oil in your left hand; if it rotates, that is good; if not, insert an needle through all the threads above; and be careful to cut along the margin of the paper where the hairs grow, cutting through all the hairs, down to the base, from the large tear to the small one. Then extract the thread, and place a small piece of cotton and cloth under the paper, and mark on the paper a figure of an anchor, as if from myrrh, but the figure should be according to the amount you raise with the paper, which is measured at all points.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you take a sharp knife and cut a great quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make incisions along all two lines that you have marked, and begin with a large drop of blood from the first incision until it becomes small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs, in the thickness of a root, then turn the point into one of the two angles towards the heart, and scrape it entirely; then bring the two edges together with a single stitch of fine flax thread, and dry the blood, and remove any excess thread from the two wounds to anything sticky, if you are able to do this. And if not, leave the stitch and the thread for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching using drying and constricting things, because paper revives at the healing of the wound and its gathering together, but stitching moves (as the ancients said), and that is a task without fear; and if in another way: it is that you mark the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have told, at three points according to the shape shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take hold of what overcomes the small forces equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the pincers, and the matter is not equal, take a needle where there is thread, and tie it around the figure; then take another thread from the large wound, and the small thread from the small one, and intertwine them equally between your fingers; then gently let go of your hand equally, and remove all the skin marked on it, as we have said; then stitch together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar remedies that ease pain; and sometimes, the hair of the paper (scab) turns. It is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one place and another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for pain in the joints is as follows: take paper and make it within this manner that I have said, then create two joints by art, and attach two thin strips as long as the paper and as broad as a spatule; bind each part where you hold the threads; then assemble them delicately on top of the paper from oil, and stretch the two joints from the formed parts; leave it thus for several days, and the pain that was constrained will die and cease, until it is resolved by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed and the pain subsides due to treatment, then cure it while it is still healthy; when the wound has healed, and if you lift the paper, and the hair does not grow back; this is the form of the two joints that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and breadth.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work requires such skill that you pierce the skin with a fine needle, and wrap it with soft and fine silk thread; then bring together the edges and tie them gently, making the length of the threads one palm's length long; then arrange in the wound another fine thread of silk quickly, tying it around the top of the thread; then place the patient's head on your healthy hand; and be careful with the sun so that the work is declared free from infection, for it is a delicate and small operation, then push the needle through all the wound to the root of the hair neatly, and pierce the paper hospital-style as you pull it away from the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the wound in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not grow with it, pull the wound out from the root along all the thread you have ordered, until the wound comes out completely through the opening above and you see it with your eye; then pull the wound and the thread, close the eye and leave it for one or two days, until the hair grows in its place and the scar is born; and if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long hair from a natural horse, and raise them with the same thread you left it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the putrefaction of the wound
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes upon the body, it appears in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from wounds, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this case is that you open the wound, separate the lips, place linen inside, and bandage it tightly until it heals; and it is not appropriate to use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but there are things that soften it, like fenugreek; and rosewater from roses, or elderflower, or flaxseed meal, cooked in oil with garlic, wrapped around it, and applied to this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the true power of this cure lies in your caution that it does not adhere strictly to its previous form; and these practices that we have mentioned are no remedy but a correct approach for this illness, so that it does not return in the same way as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the grease that comes from oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocation, truly called "fracture," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause is wound and fracture, cautery, and similar things; the outcome of these actions is such that if you prick with an needle, it has a double thread, and you insert it into the flesh, piercing from the left eyelid to the right (eye), so that the thread passes through both eyes, then the needle is above all the thread, and the eye socket is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the shape of the paper returns to what is appropriate, that's good; if not, take a razor and insert it into the opening, turn over the paper, and make two slits on each side inside the paper; let the edges of these two slits form two angles of the incision you have made, so that when they are brought together, the shape is like a letter with a "greek I" (γ); then remove the paper as much as its sides are agape from the substance beneath, and adjust both parts carefully, stitching them with a thread of linen; finally, apply the treatments we have mentioned for soothing medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from cutting or stitching or cauterizing, it is necessary that you make a clean cut between the hairs of the skin, and according to what has been said before; then separate the two books of the joint, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the skilled masters devise various means from which they can restore the figure to its natural state; and the patients themselves, according to what suits the work and the instruments in different arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	The phrase "dou soudement de la papiere" does not have a clear meaning in
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this cauterization occurs in a way that the paper (skin) is joined with white oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, it is then necessary for you to insert the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and hold it in place with pincers, as long as you remove what is hard on the delicate spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient does not suffer from the too-sharp spatula or it bleeds oil; and make your incision, by which you strip off the joined paper, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all of it is healed, and never becomes infected with salt water or strong water, but rather lifts away the foul water and replaces it with clear water and wool; and then place a linen cloth between the paper and the oil, and lay moist wool on top of the oil, and after three days use compresses and suds until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and resembles a hard, smooth stone, and another which is not nervous, but resembles white, frozen moisture, that when touched with iron and treated as if it were pincers, no one can do so; and both resemble beginning towards the great toe, and grow little by little until they cover the entire vision and all the light and movement of the finger.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The procedure for incision is as follows: the patient places his head in a healthy position, then opens the joint; takes a piece of paper and wraps it around the finger, then coils the nail like a small pincers and extends it above; takes an needle, threads it with horsehair, or goat hair, or oxen hair, and a strong thread; doubles the point of the needle slightly and pierces it through the nail, threading the entire length of the needle, and ties the nail with the thread, extending it above; then shaves off all the hair around the edge of the nail with the side of the razor, just after the cuticle, leaving only the hair on the nail itself. In this way, no tissue is damaged by the incision, as usually happens. The nail should never be extended directly using a knife, but always in the manner we have described; then the shape takes the form as follows:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be sure that the knife does not touch and tear the soft flesh, nor pierce the skin; after the incision, pour a little of the crushed silk into the wound, and bind it with a collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the fingernail is not nervous and you cannot push the needle, and the hooks cannot enter, this condition of the nail often requires medication; as I have described in the previous section, if you see it closed over the wound on the patient's hand, take a light knife according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently remove the nail from above, and if you see that it is weakening little by little and the reason is pressing, then let the liquid from your mouth fall into a colander made of lime and mixed with red wool and powdered, and stop the oil for the rest of the day; then repeat the other work according to this same process until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing in the oil contradicts you, such as a hot abscess, then apply it and treat the hot abscess first until it is healed, and then continue the work as before until it is completely cured.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh causes pain in the eye through great damage, suspending it at the corner and cutting off a part but not all, so that tears do not flow; then a red collar is distilled into the eye made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	on the flesh that is born on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people's eyes never produce a red flesh growth, which covers the eyelid and sticks to the paper-like skin, resembling a rose petal; and this condition is such that the patient places their head in a healthy position, then opens the eyelids, and gently pulls all the growths as suitable, and supports it with strength. Then, cut off the first growth, shaving everything down to the end, taking care not to irritate the eye during the procedure; and use the spatumile (a medical tool) as we mentioned for cutting under the nail and small forces to remove the flesh, as this shape demonstrates after this chapter. Once the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply a string of oil or distil red collarette into the eye, along with similar corrosive medicines, and place a piece of cotton soaked in hot oil on top; ensuring it's well secured from the aposteme (eye socket). If nothing remains and you suspect a hot aposteme, leave out the oil and treat the aposteme with calming remedies. Then, return to your procedure when everything is healed, and thus, make all the cuts adjusted in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, you must take care of each weak part of the body naturally; and in the case of an accident, with fire; and do not push your hand into any of these works until you see that this member endures the work.
des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are the red veins that are covered over the eye, they obscure the sight of their work and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Skill is most important that you first examine the eye, as it is red, swollen, and there is no other illness outside of the redness; then apply in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your healthy hand, then suspend those veins throughout their entire length according to your wisdom, and make the incisions delicate twice according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two incisions by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, gently pull the veins, wiping off the blood hour after hour until you remove them from the flesh; be careful not to puncture the oil with the edges of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, being very zealous in your task so that you do not stop until the veins are all removed; and when you have done this, distil green and red cologne into the oil to corrupt what remains from the blood.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot gather all of this in that hour, make a poultice over the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it no days until the pain is relieved and the hot abscess is assured, then begin again according to this manner as long as it is healed; and this is the form of the veins:
de la fistule de l’oil	From the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	He considers them "fistulas": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have mentioned before, and it is not healed, there is a blockage within that you must open at the abscess, where he is destined to die, and remove all moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the instruments mentioned here and shape them; it is called a "sharp blade", and it should be made from iron from the tip to the root, and pointed like a file as shown in its current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the corrupt bone back in its socket, then turn it between your fingers, and press with your hand until you know that corruption is gone; do this several times, then return the joint to its medicinal state.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joints are fused and it is born thus, and the bowel's core is also fused and remains so for 40 days without renewal or abscess, and no bad accidents occur, knowing that it is healthy; if not, there is another tool to bring the fistula back to the perforation according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and by aqueous medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the foresight according to this form, and let the iron be at three angles, and make the channel narrow up to the top as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the delicate bone of the arm, move your hand away from the wound, and continue throughout until it pierces through to the bone, and the patient feels pain in that area because of the pressure if he keeps his hand on his own; and then return to the use of dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the charred and hardened skin has formed over the bones, check for any swelling at the joint; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the wound
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound is fully open and there is no disturbance to the neck or any lessening of pain, then it is necessary that you dress the patient; first with clean bandages, then apply leech or other sucking devices without causing harm, then pour oil made from aloe, incense, and sarcocolla onto the bandages, and then strain the oil. Apply the ointment on top of cloth bands, one upon another in four layers, and then place them over the wound; the manner of the cloth bands should be that you use soft cloth enough to cover it entirely, double each layer three times, and arrange them as needed for the joint's size. Then strain a firm, hard bandage over the top and apply leeches for sucking without causing harm. Remove the leeches and leave the dressing on for a day and night, and if the wound becomes softer, that is good; if not, repeat the application of poultices, cloth bands, dressing, and leeches until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	breakage of the woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the woven fabric, it opens up and allows threads to stick out like grains of resin, which is reassuring to see; then, if you notice this, the work involves inserting a needle into the root of the affected area down to the part above, and then another needle where the thread forms a double strand from the tear; pierce the fabric with the needle, leaving the first needle in place; cut the double-stranded thread and tie a portion of the fabric around it, pulling it tightly; remove the needle and apply fresh moist lint to the wound; leave the lint on until the thread adheres to the fabric, then dress the wound with comforting items until the injury heals; and at no time should the wound be restricted by the fabric in any circular pattern until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation has a great appearance, pierce it with a delicate spatula that comes from oil, and drive out the white moisture and lower the limb, and enter again soon after; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bow of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness, called "alcunnati," is not truly water that has collected in the bowel, resembling an acute descent, but it is neither acute; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you must have the patient sit upon a seat prepared and straight, then take the head in both hands from two sides, and move it until you see the water rising above the limbs; then insert it and do not allow it to drain or disperse the light, and have the patient look at things as usual; if it does not drain below, know that it is acute, and its descent from the bowel is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you keep the patient between your hands, then take the fine instrument and make incisions on the cornea fabric along the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, until the bow is released; and when it comes out, it lets off a clear oil mixed with honey, or boiling water with fennel and honey, then apply other remedies as long as it is clean.
des aigues de l’oil	The phrase "des aigues de l’oil" translates directly to "of the waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the signs of waters in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; if it is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should place the patient's hands, with their joints crossed, between your own palms, away from direct sunlight. Apply pure and strong oil to them and hold it tightly. Take the tool called "almagda" in your right hand if the joints are on the left side of the body, or in your left hand for joint issues on the right side. Position the tool's tip along the thickest part of the skin near the smallest nerve ending, then press the magda vigorously and twist your hand as it pierces the skin. Feel when the magda reaches the empty space inside and ensures its efficacy by observing any change in color due to the clear surface of the cornified skin. The depth should be consistent with the thickness of the space between the plum stone and the end of the darkness (presumably referring to a specific anatomical structure). This is the crown of the oil. You will see the bone against the paper due to its transparent nature, then continue applying the tool along different paths, one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he lowers it now, he will see the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, he lowers the instrument a second time, applies force with it, and when it is fully inserted and does not move up again, gently extract it by turning your hand back and forth; then raise it a little bit, pulling out some of the oil from inside.
