Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply heat to the affected oil with hot wax or any other moist oily substance, and wrap it in clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place a hot poultice on it with plenty of fire.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the foreign body cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are some people whose eyelids are too tight, it is necessary that you press the instrument called 'alberit', which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva alone, and do not cut too deeply, but make it subtle, then insert the foreign body, as we have said; and after the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleep with a dark place, let him sleep on his back, and be sure of all movements, and feed him soft foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see nothing, and then put the bandage on again for seven days; and it is not appropriate that you do this during the cure or after incision now, but it is necessary to lighten the load, because acute pain mounts dangerously.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess breaks open, you should loosen the skin in front of the seventh day and apply the remedies that soothe the abscess; and when it is soothed, gradually loosen the bandage and place a slight edge on his face to cover for some time, and thereafter stay in this dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then he should gradually leave the house and return to his usual life; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iran who told us that in their peaceful lands they use a certain tool to suck out water, but I have never seen it in our land, nor do I find mention of it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of alchemy, so that whoever does not know them will see them, and they should be of gold pure.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the center of this same subtlety should be in the middle, and the three corners sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the charm on the new-born
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No one is born with these charms adjusted in various ways, so that there are none that seem like scorpions full of pain; and if there are such who have a charm adorned with bright colors, or a charm soft with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the bone is sore and not yet healed, you must place the patient's hand between your own hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, apply the hot liquid to those bones, and treat them rigorously; hold as much as you can sustain with a delicate, sharp spatula on one side, until you know that the bone is completely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is anything left that cannot be covered, open it with all the delicate and light instruments until nothing remains; without hesitation, make the incision as needed; if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the wound is completely healed and all bones are set, then apply heat or cold and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you open it and moisture comes out up to the palate, knowing that it is healthy; and if moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is a fracture in the upper bone, preventing the tools from cutting: then you must insert a thick linen thread into it, being careful with your hands, and leaving between each thread a space of equal or lesser size; and place the patient's toe in the thread at his will, and pull gently while smelling until the thread comes out through the gum inside the mouth; and often children do so at school, and it is a light task for whoever wants to do it. Then hold the gum that comes through the thread with one hand, and the other gum coming through the mouth with the other hand, knowing one after the other as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as you know, corrupt the wound with new matter, then treat the child, wipe away the blood, and moisten it with Egyptian balm; return it to the wound as before. Do this for three days or more until the balm has absorbed all that remains from the wound; then place a clean bandage on the wound for no more than a day until it is healed, and if there is need of dry medicines, use them; this is the form of the instrument for cleansing the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the wound.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it thus; if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instruments be filled to cleanse the head; have many at hand for holding the head when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, near the nose, there appears a pain called "telul" which grows and becomes very great, so much so that it is a sight to behold; and for this reason, you must treat it at the beginning, remove all bones, then apply heat or the burning medicine; and if one delays treating it until it becomes large, be careful if it has a hard, dark color, poor sensation: do not touch it with iron, as it is an abscessed joint. Because when one treats it at any time, it brings great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is sensitive to pressure, not dark in color, and you can fully treat it without causing pain or discomfort to the patient, then cure it with dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the continuance of a bone breaks into one of these powerful cartilages, it profits little, for no man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this comes to pass with no one present, then it is necessary to close the wound with two stitches, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must scrape all parts of their core while they heal, then stitch the two lips together and tighten them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and incense powder; and place a piece of plaster or other adhesive plaster over it, and leave it until it falls out by itself, and treat with ointment as it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is such that you bring the parts together: either with needles, as we have said in stitching the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, abscesses on the lips appear as hard grains, both small and large, so you must turn the lips and make a cut in each one, using forceps to extract them; then apply the vitriole (sulphuric acid) after the incision, until the wound is stained; then use an herbal compress, and care for the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	from the work of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a growth appears on the gums, which the old call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with pincers and cut it at its root, allowing the bowel or abscess to drain; then apply powdered vitriol or other drying and constricting powders; and if the growth returns after the incision, this happens often, especially if the root is cut again and cauterized; if it does not return after cauterization, these are the shapes of the instruments used for cutting.
des sordens	from disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth are ever aligned at the top of the jaw, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and no tooth is black and yellow and rotten until the corruption reaches the gums, and the tooth becomes bad-smelling. It is necessary that you hold the patient's jaws in your hands, and their teeth should be in your safe keeping, and file the teeth or gums that are visible, as long as nothing remains; and so do with black, green, jaundice, and other stains until they are clean. If what is on the first surface is removed, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and third, until everything is filed; and know that teeth require various types of tools to file, according to what the work shows, because the tool used to remove teeth from between them has a different shape than the one used to file them. And these shapes and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should treat the tooth when it causes pain, and do so as quickly as you can, for no one should delay; for it is a very precious substance indeed, hence there is no excuse for procrastination.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is in great pain, it is important that you be certain about which tooth is painful.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient complains of pain, and you must be certain which tooth is causing it, and pull the good tooth, but nevertheless, the pain does not cease until the bad tooth is extracted, as we have already seen with these healthy teeth; and when you are quite certain about the painful tooth, you should scrape gently around the tooth in all directions to protect the gums, then move the pliers quickly and precisely at the first chance, while keeping them firmly gripped, and pull the tooth out between your knees, holding it tightly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it doesn't come out, take none of these instruments and push them gently from every side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is broken and pulled out, it is necessary that you fill the space with cloth, either at the opening or the gap; and if it is tightly held by pliers, be careful not to break it while pulling; and it is very important to work skillfully around the gums to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be very careful so as not to break it, and if a part breaks off, return the remaining piece to the patient, for due to the evil of the root, he will experience greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, by their haste and audacity, often break the bandages, and do not apply what we have described; but they sometimes bring on a great illness due to their imprudence or because of the bandages they break, as we have often seen; and when the wound is raw, wash it with wine or honey and lint; and the pus flows, which often happens, use vitriole powder; if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which to mute the tooth first, should be long and thin with robust handles, so as not to bend when you pull the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let the members be of good size so they do not bend when pulled, and well-forged of iron, and toothed for proper movement.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck when pulled, it is necessary to place a moistened piece of cotton or butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	while the eyes remain soft, then one applies pliers called "algefri", which make the teeth appear as if they are being cared for; and they are made inside like a file and have this shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge from these clutches, it is necessary that you uncover the skin all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", which is a pliers, in this way:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very strong and does not break, and the root jumps out by itself, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, and the shapes will come as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two prongs, the shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are used in the reason of teeth, and this instrument that seems like great pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	This instrument should be strong so it does not break, and you should know that many instruments for teeth exist; and also other tools, which are not mentioned. The most skilled surgeons invent their own instruments, according to what their work and the disease show them, because there are many diseases for which no instrument was taught in olden times. If one breaks or is unable to hold onto another bone or object, and needs an instrument I have described, then... (the text describes a process without completing the sentence).
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-hold the bone, that it does not escape but can hold and extract; and then return to the use of appropriate medicines for this, and if there is rot in the bone, small or large, remove it with all these tools.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural shape of the body, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the other teeth and is not in the right place, and one cannot cut or file it. Then extract it; and if it is loose with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape resembles a small beak, and make it very sharp:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the surgeon should hold the tooth firmly in his hands day after day for its hardness, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as the shape requires.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also done with the file as they make needles; file the tooth day after day gently, so it does not move until it is ready; then, at the end, any roughness must be filed down, and if the tooth is too sharp, it can damage the tongue, so you must file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not injure or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth aches.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches severely, either from percussion or pulling, and the patient cannot press on it without pain, then medicines restricting it are useless. They should be restrained with a gold thread, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never does; and the thread should neither be too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you need to direct the teeth, take the thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then place the aching tooth(es) between the healthy ones, one or more, until you reach gently and carefully to the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering until you reach the point where you began, and pull your hand gently and carefully until it does not move. Ensure the thread is at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the bones with a pair of pliers, and assemble them, and reconnect them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not damage the tongue; and then leave it as tight as possible while it heals, and if it disconnects, the thread will pull from another thread; if it heals and serves thus for all its time, this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the correct placement of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is dislodged, it should be replaced in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said; and it should not be handled by anyone who is not skilled and patient, and never should one make the shape of a tooth from the bone of a sheep, and place it in the gap where the defect is, and tighten it as we have said, and let it heal for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut off the language's loose ends.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No matter what kind of these connections that come from beneath the tongue, whether natural or by deep wound accident; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient with pain, and hold his head securely in your hands, and pull out the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or something else, and it comes suddenly from a wound, if it twists the hook and cuts wide that ligament; and be careful not to cut too deep into the split, for the artery that is beneath; and when you have done this, gently raise the affected limb with rosewater or oil, or cold water, then place a thin cloth under the tongue; and repeat this for each patient at night, so that the muscles do not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the discharge of pus occurs, place a hot poultice on it; and if the fever leaves, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is red or black or hard, so the patient does not smell it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it turns pale, and there is moisture in it, drain it with a fine spatula on both sides; and if the fever leaves at your work, place a hot poultice on it as long as it is stained, then return to your work until you treat everything completely. Then remove the poultice gently and from side to side, and apply other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No single time does a hole appear in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the II amandres, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if they are small and of a pale color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also because of the blood flow; but leave it until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break on its own. And if they are white in color and the root is thin, have a ready instrument to cover it, but first make sure that the abscess is calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient stand before the sun, and stretch his limbs to their full extent, opening the mouth wide and gripping the teeth with both hands, pressing the tongue down firmly against the instrument, from which this shape will be formed; it should be of silver or fine gold, like a sharp knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You should not press the tongue against all of this instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the bone hook and file it in the groove, pulling it upwards as far as possible; do not touch any part of the strings with it, then cut it with the instrument, forming a shape that resembles a forceps; nevertheless, the jaws are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if you make it with pliers, like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And it should be cut on one side and not the other; and when you have extracted one of the mandibles, extract the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's mouth with hot water and cold water and salt, and if there is bleeding, rinse the patient's mouth with pomegranate peels or mulberry leaves or similar things until the blood stops; then treat it while it is still fresh; and no other abscesses will form in the throat besides these two mandibles, so extract them just as you did the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was in her throat, namely a small abscess; and had she tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could not eat or drink, she would have died if she remained that way for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced two ribs through the two openings in the throat where it entered.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a needle into one of the openings and drew it out through the other, and cut a large portion from it; then I re-inserted the needle into the other opening and opened up the throat and pressed the tongue; after that, I probed these abscesses and extracted some of their contents, and only a little blood came out; and so the passageway in the throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut into the abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large. Then I sewed it up and cauterized it inside the throat; in this way it healed without growing again; and from these treatments, and after my departure, only God knows what happened to her.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eyeball descends and is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thin and round, it is called "eye.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess is calm, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to drain it; and the round one that is not distant; and it is bloody or of a dark color, then it is necessary to avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the sick person.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So it is necessary, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, to lay the patient before the sun and press the tongue with the instrument of which we spoke above; then insert the pin in the eye and pull it out from the back, and cut off the tendon with one of the two instruments I mentioned for the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut off more than the excess beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it causes great pain to the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we said regarding the incision of the two mandibles, and treat it as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you use an instrument for cauterizing the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization is very acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head on a healthy surface and then press the tongue with the instrument mentioned in this chapter of cauterization (as described below), using sharp, hot iron. It should not be too thick or too thin; and apply the weight of this instrument in such a way:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the physician have a brush, as if it were the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and have the patient lie on his side, so that saliva and mucus from his mouth can absorb the medicine, so it does not go down to the throat and cause irritation. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for the amount of half an hour, until you see it stop seeping and the pain from the medicine is eased; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, dip the cotton in the medicine, and insert it into the hollow of the eye, pressing it against the cotton until it dries on the eye. Do this several times until the cauterization is complete, then leave it to dry, and after three or four days, or five, if you need to repeat the cauterization, do so again, wiping the instrument around the eye with cotton dipped in medicine, and cleaning what is around the medicine; then rinse with cold water and use gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than cauterization, and it is more effective with incision; if it is treated with fumigation in this way, take plenty of calament, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avern (or fennel), and similar herbs, and mix all or any of them together in a pot, and add water, and boil it; the pot should be well sealed with a tight lid, and have a cheveit (a kind of strainer or sieve) placed over it, as described above.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be either of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be squeezed in the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye becomes numb; after that, it often recurs as long as the eye is dry. Be careful not to perform this at the beginning of a hot abscess, as various complications may arise; and do not attempt this except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a stick and put a piece of ice in the mouth of the patient, so that it is not too hot; for the piece of ice does not allow the vapour to heat the mouth, and this is a good remedy overall.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often, a sore throat is caused by bone or fish spine, or some other object. Therefore, you should treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument so that you may observe the thing. And if it does not open and is stuck in the throat, it is good to make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread, and then you should tie a thread to the sponge and pass it through (the throat); and when it reaches the place, it will open, and then you should pull it out forcefully. And if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And take the curved instrument to the throat so that it can enter more easily, and raise the head; be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that all of it does not come out, nor push the bone inside; and move the patient to insert the instrument, because it needs to be moved where the object is loose; if it goes down, pull it back with equal force throughout the instrument until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	regarding the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No treatment with medicine should be given to the throat, as I said in the previous section, except with medicinal remedies; and if that does not help, then look at the throat of the sick person in the light of day, and press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, draw it out with all its small pins, or subtle pliers that are fit for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a sheep's gut, insert it into the throat of the patient with the disease, then twist or lift the gut in hot water and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient suffers from fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take many glasses of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in, swallowing it all, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will close.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, and the patient inhales the noxious fumes from the instrument used in the fumigation of the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually break without warning.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: You should press a pot with hot coals in it, and place a perforated cover over it so that the smoke escapes from the holes. The patient then puts the end of the pipe in his mouth and closes his mouth, allowing the smoke to enter but preventing it from escaping; this continues until the smoke has had its effect. If the smoke does not break through (i.e., the patient does not sneeze), repeat the fumigation multiple times. The patient should endure thirst and eat salty, spicy foods, and avoid drinking water. Then, it will be necessary to expel the smoke from his body in this manner.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if you can see it, resembles a curved claw that enters the throat; it looks like a bird's beak and has the roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and here is its appearance:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to the memory that comes from this book, and they differ in opening and size; and there are two manners, one is in its same appearance, and of those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess on the upper part of the body is different from that at its base, and the abscess of the fleshy parts of the limb is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if at abscesses one must not pierce while the bowel is still alive according to its completion; and if of such it is necessary to pierce when they are grown hard, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are in joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from damaged joints, and it is left until it becomes gangrenous around, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is in the main member, and you delay the incision until it becomes gangrenous, it will harm the principal member; or if it is in the foundation, you must perforate it similarly as it is gangrenous, otherwise it will spread throughout, forming a fistula, and it cannot heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of perforation of the abscess, which is killed according to completion; and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness decrease, and the swelling in the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the perforation depend more on the abscess, where it opens; and it should be a long perforation through the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equally where there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there are abscesses in the fatty parts of the body, it is better to leave the incision until the swelling has subsided after the digestive process, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it too soon, the body will be filled with venom from it, and it will be full of filth; and by chance, the lips may harden and become attached to it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that is pierced according to the thickness of the body, as needed by the member.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must treat small abscesses with small incisions; for large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if it is necessary to dig out the heart, and cover; when it has healed as much as cloths, and is softened, then one must do the same as with buboes: and if they are split into three angles, or such that one covers them like a sheet of myrtle, or like abscesses from attacks; and if there is a need for a large cut, and other cuts and similar removals.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, like a superficial abscess, you must pierce it thoroughly; and if the abscess is large, and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, then do not drain all of the pus at once, but drain a part; then stop the abscess for the next day, and then drain nothing more from it; repeat this many times, gradually, until all the pus has drained; especially if the patient is weak, or a woman, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For often the patient jumps with fear at the sound of the bow, which may cause the sick to die, and you will not be blamed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be very careful with this chapter: when you have noticed your abscess, if the wound is clean, apply a thin layer of linen or cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, then insert a thin piece of cloth so that it touches each other; and if you find a part of hard skin in the abscess and you have closed it around, then fill it with dry cotton or linen rags without moisture, and leave it for three days; then open it and apply the cure until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flow occurs due to the operation, apply cold water and ice, and moisten the compress, and place it over the bleeding joint repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply a compress with medicines as mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, or the joint and abscess are very sensitive, you must place moistened linen and drapes on them. If it is summer, and the joint is fleshy, put moistened linen and drapes soaked in vinegar and hot oil; do this for three days as we have said. Then, remove the abscess and clean and dress it as appropriate until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: so I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and now see this chapter.
des soros	from sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or sometimes the chief sickness comes from small abscesses, and they are like threads, also like the sinew of a goose, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are thick and such that have moisture like pulsations; and if there are any of these that are hard and difficult to cut through, then it is certain that the artery does not prevent them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the trunk is such that you should try all instruments called "intrusive", from which the shape below comes, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, it scrapes off nothing leaving the skin that contains the moisture, for it returns repeatedly if you leave nothing; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, use water and string, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will cure what has been delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin again with the bandage, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know for certain that it does not stay in place at night; then treat the wound with suitable medicament until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if an abscess persists firmly, following this form, for a long time; and it gushes pus, and the skin is peeled from all sides, and you use every effort to drain the cloth where it resides; and if the artery causes difficulty, then do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess that is persistent and hard, cutting and treating it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And make an incision above the abscess and around it, if it is softer, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses or pimples, and it is one of these hard abscesses that I have found on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, sharp and white, and it cannot be crushed; and if anyone were to try to break it, they would do no better than cutting into stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that appear on the head, especially those coming from the roots of the ears, keep the opening completely open as long as necessary for the pus to drain; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and dissolves the adhesions, and attacks the angles, and never occurs elsewhere on the body, and it is painful, and twisted upon itself.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is strictly within its ribcage, as we have said, both the nodule and the abscess from the head, and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some of them contain moisture, and there are others that are malicious and refuse to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that which you see of good disposition to touch, and it resembles the color of healthy flesh, and is silent from every side and not dry as the nails of the finger or the artery or the duct, and is not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape from every part, and the two lips of the heart be intact, if you have need, as we have said in the chapters on the head; and take your time, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not let the fingers slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, put in the wound vitriole (a poisonous substance) ground into powder, or any powders that stop blood, and close the wound; and leave it until the inflammation is calmed, and the wound softened, and begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work until you complete it; then pay attention to your careful indication if there remain no small sores, clean and healed.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the sore, it is not enough that you merely cut off the sore at its root, but you should tie it with a double strong thread and leave it to fall without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut off the entire sore, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the sore.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you need to understand how to deal with the root of the issue, pull it out forcefully, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofulas with excessive buildup, puncture them where they appear to be paling; and do so as mentioned before, depending on the situation, then apply these remedies with ointment and similar measures, so that it does not corrupt what is left from the infection; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue the treatment with the ointment until it heals.
de squinance	squinance (n.) - squint or cross-
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They spoke and wrote about the treatment of the throat; but I have never seen anyone perform it in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squint (strabismus), it is necessary to avoid the throat slit known as "epiglottis"; no aid should be provided through this method, because all the veins and the pores that carry the patient's illness are in those who have abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it in three circles or four small incisions across, between the two circles, or according to the depth of the incision, not touching the cartilage; and these cuts are very suitable for the section of the epiglottis as there is no charring, and the edges remain long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeon is cautious, he must extend the throat skin completely around the ring, then cut the heart until it reaches the trachea; and avoid blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut according to what we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the river of the trachea that jumps out from the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound towards the heart, and cut through them entirely where the cartilage is; then administer medications that promote healing as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim understands that one must not proceed until the throat is completely sealed, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, lacking all hope.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then one should remove the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe otherwise, and they will breathe through the wound, thus being kept from dying; and for this reason, the ancients commanded that the wound remain open until the evil of the illness has passed, either in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and dress it, as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel was pierced by a knife, and it entered her throat, cutting part of the duct from the womb; and I was called to cure her, but I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it; I realized that there was no proper vein or channel leading to the throat, but the veins were emerging from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I acted quickly, sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; then the damsel recovered her voice, and returned to her normal state; therefore I say that one should not be afraid when dealing with the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cystic abscesses are called "neck hernias", and they are large abscesses in the color of a jasper, and they are common in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental, where the natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two ways: one is similar to fat, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; it inspires fear and should not be operated on with fire except in a small case where, if you find it like fat and there is no way out, you treat it as you would treat a nose, removing it completely, if necessary, and wrapping it well, curing it as appropriate until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways in which we can approach this subject, of which I will describe all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I explain the entire distinction between origin and outcome.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the outcome is fever and heat-holding as long as the ebullition (boiling) has not occurred, and it completes its putrefaction; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new (growth/condition), there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains satisfaction (or healing), which is its own sac, and follows the state of the body, and begins like a wound, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either oily or moist, and have much the same color as I described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to the treatment of a new patient, first try and inquire about all the instruments called "entromissory", according to their form, as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of inquiring about abscesses is to press more or less moistly on the abscess you find, and move your fingers in and out little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the core; then, according to the size of the abscess, extract the entromissory, and be careful not to allow it to slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.
