If the abscess is surrounded by a hard crust, of the color I described for other abscesses, then do as I said before for other abscesses; but if after removing the entromissory, no moist discharge appears, know that it is full of pus, so make a cross over it and hold it with pincers, scraping off the crust gently from all sides, and take care to remove the core where it lies, making sure you leave nothing behind. And if you cannot remove it whole, cut it into pieces so as not to leave anything behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays put, the pain returns again and again; and if it lingers a little while causing no great distress, it uses some corrosive powders or hot water to open the wound, tightens the wound, applies soothing things to the abscess, and treats it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the pain persists, it cuts both sides of the wound and treats it according to what causes it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pain persists or something else causes you haste, use vitriol powder and leave it for two or three days until the wound pus forms, and rests from the fever of the blood; then come back to cover what has fallen away again.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments introduced, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quadrants called "albaret", and one called "breb", and they are also like needles with which one sews up wounds, made of brass, iron, or silver, and move best those that are yellow, and are most tried for encircling the abscesses of fistules; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the opening of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks with two curves in three ways; and there are hooks with three curves, also in three ways; and there are hooks with two curves, and some with only one curve, in three ways; all these are necessary for their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments is sharp, and there are some that do not cut completely through, leaving the skin intact, so as not to sever the vein or nerve; and these introducers have the blades reposed in several pieces, so that the patient does not lose them when opening the abscesses. And they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they should only be used on fleshy parts like legs, arms, breasts, wounds, and similar places; and never make a smaller tool resembling the cuts of fists, according to this form, with which one stops the blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that severs veins and arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflame the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like a woman's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them must do so according to this form described in this line b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicinal herbs with charred ash, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and heal it as long as it remains healthy; and if the mammary tissue slopes downward, and softens because of its size, as happens in women, making them seem to have two ridges on top, through these similar fissures; so that one holds onto the other at the end of each, making the larger line contain the smaller according to this form from line b to g. Then scrape off the leather between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we've said about stitching and powders, as well as anything necessary for healing while it remains healthy; and if it's not healthy, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood oozing, it's necessary to fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing; leave it until it absorbs the fat and moisture, then cure it as long as it remains healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulous nodules or they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply clean cotton to the wound and leave it for another day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with suitable medicine until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then it should be treated as we have said about the cuts in scrofula, and if the wound gapes, then apply cautery as we have previously stated.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery ruptures and the membrane (cuir) above it severs, it often leads to abscesses, and sometimes the vein becomes inflamed and also develops an abscess; and if one recognizes this as due to an artery rupture, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it at your extremities, you feel a strange sensation; and in the case of the vein, there is intense pain and obvious swelling; and it is foolish to attempt to treat such an abscess, especially when it is deeply lodged among adhesions and angles and various other joints, and it becomes very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should seek iron cautery, and he who is in charge should also be vigilant, and on whoever has an artery opening cut deeply into the flesh; then skillfully remove the artery with a single thread in two parts, as I taught you for extracting the two arteries found in the temples; then mark the spot between the two threads of an instrument until all moisture leaves, and treat the abscess; then administer treatment as soon as the link is strong; and cure any subsequent care as appropriate, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to a vein cut, hold onto your hand what you can of the abscess to the entire skin, then push the needle from below the spot you hold in your hand, and pierce it, creating a double thread so that you draw it from the other side; then secure the abscess as I instructed you, or bind it to one of the two parts of the thread; and if you doubt the threads have left, insert another needle through all the abscess below the first cut, and tighten the threads in three parts; then cut away the excess until the necessary part is removed, then cut away the excess flesh around the wound, and leave what is bound; then place a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, and administer further treatment and care until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscess of the nail
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly to how abscesses occur in arteries and veins, nails can also develop abscesses when they are injured or subjected to excessive work, among other things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more frequently in nails and toes where there are joints, which is a source of great abscesses, and their appearance seems to be the color of the skin, and they take various forms with intense pain; and when they form, the patient feels severe pain, and it is not fully healed within the body, but only beneath the heart; and it moves from all sides, neither advancing nor retreating, neither downwards nor upwards, and those in joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps they would contract; and those on the head or forehead cause the skin to split.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it holds a nail, cut it at its base; and if it's large, suspend it with a hook, then peel off the skin, next remove the bone, and sew up the wound, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	The phrase "des grosses boces pendans" translates roughly to "hanging large
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It never appears in the stomachs and nowhere else, it is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance, it has subtle roots, large droppings; and there are both small and very large ones; and I have seen men who had two or three such growths in their bellies which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had thin roots, were continually moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I gathered them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 З. (unclear unit), and the work of the incision is such that if you look at the patient, they are moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of delicate root; if it is cut with a wide spatula, and let the fire cautery be in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting, many serious consequences of blood loss occur, and if you are slow, cauterize immediately; and if you see the patient hoping and fearful of the incision, take a well-made plug of thread, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop pulling on the thread until it cuts through the artery, without effort; and if the roots are thick, be afraid to cut them, especially in the stomach, but you can still cut half of them, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the thin part that is red, poor in blood, and milky in appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enhanced, and I will come to the treatment of cancer hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed due to crusting.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the crust comes from cauterization of the wound or fissure of the tissue, and it is on the abdomen and in none of the bowels, as happens in other openings, or from a cancer that cuts veins or arteries according to what is above, or from putrefaction; and if it is through the rupture of the soft tissue and through the emission of the bowels, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a slight thing without pain, and opens through various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an intestinal issue, then it is more complex, and when pressed at the patient's will, it rebounds, and sometimes becomes tightened, greatly constricting the entry to the bath and causing much effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue and opens easily when pressed in the hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed in quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it feels soft upon touching, and the strain is such that you must observe its appearance, whether it is due to the blood of an artery, a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter about abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be related to the intestine or bowel, then you must instruct the patient to retain their excrement, and lie completely straight, then mark around the entire opening; then command them to twist carefully between your hands, then re-enter the wound at the place you have marked with all the sputum, then stretch half of the abscess above all the major sinew; then tie it firmly with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk, and make sure the nerves are completely relaxed; then open the other half of the abscess stretched over the thread, and insert your finger to explore the intestine; if you find it caught in the thread, untie it and pull out the intestine from beyond the stomach; and if you find the bowel, at the sinew, cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, gently twist around, then return to your work, take two needles, and insert them through what you have made in the form of a cross that you made pierce; then stretch the abscess three parts above the needles, and if you see it recede, remove the needles, leave the wound to heal, and cut off the dead flesh by yourself; or you can cut it when it becomes soft and rotten, then cure the wound as necessary, and complete the abscess as we have said; then extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound appropriately, and close the opening.
dou chancre	A cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the previous section the various types of ulcers, and how they should be treated with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; we say that an ulcer becomes acute in a bad place, and requires great caution in its treatment, and advise the ancients that when an ulcer is located where it can be cut out, as in the flesh of animals, or in the foot, or in similar places, it should all be removed when it is in the beginning; but when it is large and old, you must not even approach it, for I have never been able to make anyone well from such an ulcer; nor has anyone ever been cured by me before.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the work, when an ulcer is located where it can be removed, as we have said, you must never purge the patient of black blood; then make the wound healthy if there is clear repletion; then cut out the ulcer in a good place to perform the operation; then pour on your poultices or ulcers, and shave all parts, removing any remaining pus; let the blood flow completely, and feel the place with your hand or anything else; if the occurrence of blood makes you hesitate when incising an artery or vein, cauterize it until the wound is cleansed; then apply another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	From hydropsie (a condition marked by excessive fluid accumulation
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the similarities of hydropsie (a condition marked by excessive fluid accumulation) and described how the buildup of fluid occurs, the symptoms of each type, and the treatments using medicine and iron. In these two cases - tympanites and yposarche - iron should not be used, as it is a dangerous thing; however, when treating this hydropsie-like condition called "eclites" with medicines, if the patient's weakness or other illnesses like intestinal distension or similar conditions are in question, do not use iron due to uncertainty. If you observe a strong and healthy patient suffering only from hydropsie, without any other illness, you should proceed as follows: place the patient comfortably on your hands, press the abdomen towards the lower part using a sharp-pointed spatula, according to this form...
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, but not so deeply that it reaches the intestines when inserted, and do not let it burst; then observe if there is any droplet formation towards the intestines. You should make your incision three finger-breadths deep directly under the armpit, and if the drops are due to liver disease, make your cut on the left side of the armpit; and if it's from the urinary tract, on the right side, and do not let the patient lie on the incision so that the surplus does not flow into the weak part. Then, with a tool, pierce through all the skin and the underlying tissue, and gently apply your hand to all the pus between the skin and the abscess as if you were shaving it down to the thickness of a fingernail or slightly more; then continue piercing the abscess until the pus flows out freely, which is the sign for water (or clear liquid). Then drain it and remove this tool, and this is the shape [of the incision].
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of fine gold or bright silver, and has a small opening at its center; on one side, three openings; and two on the other, and one on the third. And the part is cut as a feather, and this is the shape of the incision in which the scribes cut the feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it sinks immediately onto the instrument; then empty half or a third, for if you empty more than is necessary at this time, perhaps the patient dies due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls into a coma, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses. Then take the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held back now by the kernel that stops up the opening which I have mentioned, so you pierce in this manner; then continue the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw out a small quantity of water; do this for several days, and beware of letting it stagnate until only a little bit of water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water, whether it be by the cure of a grave or hot earth, or much sweating or bath, or in the sun, and turned to drinking; and treat with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said above.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary at any time for him not to pierce through all the very subtle particles according to this form.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then open the subtle closure of the bladder, and hold it closed for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the closure, let him urinate, and then replace it; but sometimes this is not necessary, because the force of the urine that comes out will not allow it to remain closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the closure is small, it is a sign of a weak bladder, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the perforation in their place are blighted, for no one is born with a perforation at the top of the organ, so they cannot urinate until they raise their organ; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach up to the end, and it is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, then the head of the organ and the opening are also as thick as a pen, so that the perforation can be made in the middle, as it should; and beware of the bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops the bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this affliction appears on the penis, and it manifests in a foul manner; it can be either malignant or benign. You must probe them gently with a fine needle, scrape and clean them thoroughly, then apply moist cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; continue to treat the wound with diaphoretic ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the affliction is malignant, with a putrid and foul appearance, it requires cautery treatment.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have achieved it, and if the splint is in a crooked position, with part of it inside the skin and part sticking out, then you must remove the splint that is inside first; and when it is loosened, then apply the treatment externally.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless you are certain that the position of the splint is not damaged, blackening and decay will occur in the splint and bone; therefore, remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from honey and flour consisting of grated red apples and leaves, and continue treatment with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a blood clot comes, then instruct the lunar cauterizer according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterizer should assist in two ways: that is to say, at the onset of blood clotting and corruption; and if the tip of the instrument is corrupted and withdrawn, then it is necessary to push or direct the instrument a little deeper, and let the patient urinate; and when the hair on top of the instrument's head has fallen off for those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or abscess, it is then necessary to peel it with a sharp instrument until the ligaments are loosened, and all parts of the instrument's tip are released; and if this task is too difficult to plan, it is better to peel it with a spatula at the very top of the instrument and the stone; then gently separate them, and place a thin, moist linen cloth in cold water directly on it so that no hair grows back.
de la circoncision	On circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not dislocation of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and most gentle work for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not practice it in their laws, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and elders who practiced circumcision in those days, and they did it with force and at any cost; it was dangerous because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts through this one, they might damage that one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns with the cover, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleansing which is from far away, the point of the member is not assured; and in the cleansing of the nail, by chance, the iron escapes, and it corrupts the work, and often arises so that they do not need cleansing and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing that is done with force on all the fibrous threads, I have found the benefit of experience, for the forces cut exactly as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, if you cut it evenly in all directions, the thread should be well twisted around the skin; and make sure the first movement is such that the child, if it listens, understands that you are not tightly binding the thread around the stick, but rather loosening it in all ways as much as possible; then stretch it between your hands straight, and distribute the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand on the stick and blow into its heart, and pull it up until the end of the stick is together; then clean it well from the dirt that has accumulated, then tie a double knot at the joint marked with a thread, then tie it below to another thread; and hold it by both ends in the second knot on the pouche and the index finger, and cut between the two threads, then lift the heart gently from above cruelly, pull the chief of the stick; then let the blood drain drop by drop, for that is how it heals; and apply powder on top, and cover with a cloth glued with a half-cooked egg white mixed with rose water, confit with good red oil and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and continue treatment as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of purification is as follows: both shoulders should be bare and cut open, and the shoulder blades should also be large and evenly sized.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification occurs when the blood vessels inside are cut; then you should extend your finger so that the joint becomes swollen; and also the wound, if you cannot hold it with your fingers, use pincers, and then close the wound.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they remain for three days, and what is under the stick is swollen, leave it until the abscess has healed, gently peeling off the skin; close the wound as much as you can, and protect the area around the stick; this will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the place suddenly afflicted with a wound from powder, which we have spoken of in treating powders, and if one takes too much care, it will go to excess, without harming; treat it then, as we have said, while it is sound.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a stillborn child, or similar conditions, as we have discussed in the previous section; and if the urine cannot be released, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, it is necessary for the patient to be positioned sitting on his knees; and pressure should be applied to his back, and he should bend his belly upwards from below the back, and restrain him as much as possible. And then the neck of the bladder is forced against the stone above, allowing the urine to flow; if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary for you to perform an extraction using a syringe, which has the form of: a thin, light silver needle, about one palm and a half in length, fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of urination is as follows: take a double thread and tie one end to a ball of wool or cotton, then insert the free end into the syringe; cut off the excess wool and insert it back up to the top of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg albumen, and place the patient on a couch. Raise the bladder and the urethra with moist oil and olive oil and warm water, then gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of the urethra. Double the urethra over itself towards the opening, then withdraw the syringe before the bladder, and let the patient feel the urine flow until the bladder is empty. If it does not follow this order, because the direction in which the thread goes leads to a twist, then cut the thread piece by piece, and the urine will follow the thread, then extract it gently and drain the urine; repeat the process with the syringe until the bladder is completely emptied, and ease the patient's discomfort.
des maladies de la vessie	Of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or pus comes to the bladder, where putrefaction is assembled, you should view it distill water and medicines, by using the entire instrument called 'clepsydra', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; and the hair of the neck by which the medicine cuts so well the penis without addition, if one can drain the moisture and push as needed; and when you see your medicines gushing into the bladder, place the head of the instrument in the moisture and draw out the liquid that is inside. Draw it out gently, then firmly push back the piston; the moisture will enter the instrument and immediately go to the bladder, so the patient will feel it; and this is the shape of the delicate enema bag used to enema the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the matter is more precious; then open the wound beneath the breast; take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you wish to use for enema; tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat this moisture over fire. Then insert the head of the enema into the anus, and press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture enters the bladder, as long as the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder. If you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make it circular, and pierce it roundly; then thread a strong string through these holes, assemble the circle like a ring, and place within it oil, moisture, and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods for treating stones and their extraction, along with various medicinal approaches; I have also explained the distinction between stones that are rainy and those that are not, as well as the signs to look for, and what type of stone requires surgical intervention, whether in the bladder or the urethra. And I will now convey this information to you clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is rainy in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign of acute uric acid from the bladder, appearing in its subtlety; it opens up their urethra, greatly tormenting them, often recurring, and then hardening; and much of this leads to destruction. The healing process for children is lighter until they reach four years old, and it is much more severe for the elderly, falling somewhere in between for those between youth and old age. The treatment is also lighter for those with larger stones compared to those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a enema, in order to expel all feces from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often gets stuck when trying to pass a stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and debounce them, and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, without sticking in the upper part; then place him between your hands with his legs down, so that the bladder is tilted downward; then stop and feel inside. If you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come away at the touch of anything, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and press on the patient, or use your middle finger for a younger, fully grown patient; push it back into its socket, hold it in place, and when you feel it in your right hand, if it is at the base of the bladder; then press firmly on your right side, and pull it out to the outside where you see it has been cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards and spread apart the lips, and with his left hand remove the skin that lies beneath the lips at the point where the incision is made; then he should insert the spatula completely, which forms its shape.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make an incision between what is between the scrotum and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and it should be straight on the stone, and both legs should be either on the fundament or elevated, and the cut should be wide at the beginning and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; so that the pressure from the leg which is on the fundament forces it out without effort; and know that there are stones with angles and margins: this one is difficult to pass; and if it's in a place below, resembling a nail, and round, its issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you need to use pliers that are also like a file at the top to extract the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you can insert a thin, curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot do this, enlarge the opening slightly, and if the stone is covered with skin, extract it with vitriol; and if there are several stones, first remove the largest one from the bladder's neck, then cut around it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must cut it out carefully, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine flows again through the limb that the joints cannot hold together; but nevertheless, make every effort to extract it, either with pliers or by piecing it out, until you have finished. Then apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bandage it, placing a moist cloth of oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, on the hot abscess to soothe it. Then bind the patient tightly to his bed for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of hot and cold oil and water arises, then apply curative ointment and basic ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosion and congeals of blood in the bladder occur, and urination is hindered in this way: then press your finger into the wound, extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause illness; then cleanse the wound with water and salt and herbs, and assist in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and remember that every time you treat it, you should bind both thighs together and apply medicines to the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is caught in the urethra, and stuck inside, and urine cannot pass; then if you treat this as I say, cutting it many times, that should be an excuse for the cutting by this method.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tried this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the first piece of iron according to this form and insert it at three angles into one tisson.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra beyond the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently push the bore into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the bore in your hand slowly into the stone, as much as you can, piercing the stone from another side; and soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is often broken and jumps with urine, and it irritates the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that defies you, then take a needle and thread, and sew through the stone from below and above, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the string, and clean the frozen blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones" (a reference to kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare for women to have stones, and if they do, the treatment is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is hard to find a knowledgeable woman who understands how to expose herself properly, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. And the third way is that by chance one may not find a woman well-versed in this art of surgery; and the fourth way is that the woman's stone is often more difficult to pass than the man's, so it needs to be cut deeper, and great fear is involved. And if necessity calls for it, it is right to hire a skilled midwife, and if you cannot find one, then choose a clever woman in women's lives, or a woman who knows part of this art, and command her to do what you order regarding the examination of the stone; and look very carefully to see if that woman is a virgin. Then she should push down her leg to seek the stone, and if she finds it, she should constrain it from above with her leg, and advise her to push her left hand down onto the swollen bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If it is cut, it is necessary that she moves the stone little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the thigh, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the kidney, where it is moved and felt, and do not move the stone above or below the kidney, and make a small incision in the first place; then turn the rat into the incision, if you feel the stone so hard in the wound that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	knowing these similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound does not heal, put powdered glass on it and keep it there for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work while the stone is still firm, and have the tools I told you for extracting stones from men to aid you in your task; and if the wound does not heal, and it is an artery that is cut, sprinkle powder on the area and bandage it with several bandages and do not repeat this, leave the stone and do not pull it out unless the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the swelling goes down, then return to your work while the stone is still firm.
de hernie carnouse	from hernia carnous
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rices water (or white fluid) is nothing other than the accumulation of moisture or white matter, which is located beneath the skin, containing the egg white, and is called "syphac," never properly part of the egg white itself; and this is the thin membrane between the white matter and the inner skin. This does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this rice is due to weakness in the skin, which causes it to spread and accumulate matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it arise from a percussion on the joints, and this moisture can take many forms: it might be yellow, or without red, or black, or pale white, and so on; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, the abscesses are bright, quite long like the shape of a goose feather, and do not open the joints, because they are filled with moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the entire joint, the abscesses are bright with a part of the bone, and it is thought to be another bone; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white substance, it smells well; then, when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine all the inner parts, as mentioned above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows, judge of what is inside after the introduction.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then place him on his back, on something slightly elevated, and put many sheets under him; then sit on his left side and command the assistant to sit at his right, and extend the stick to one of the two ribs near the heart of the chest; then take the scalpel, and cut through the skin of the ribs from top to bottom down to the knuckle, and make the incision completely straight by judging the skin of the ribs up to a satisfactory white, and remove it gently according to the skill of the surgeon; then pierce the tissue plain with water at a wide opening, and extract all the water, and then apply your fingers, and pull the tissue upwards; and do not touch the heart of the rib, but only the tissue; cut around him carefully, in pieces or whole, as is best; if you do not cut it thoroughly, the water will return; and if the effusion has ceased to your satisfaction, put him back in his place when you have completed the work on the tissue. Then sew together the two books of the ribs with a stitch, and treat it like other wounds until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to hold the vessels that are suspended, in doubt about the flow of blood; then cut off the clot from the entire suspension, and extract the blood, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts, each with its own branch; then cut off the other part just as you did with the first, rinse it with blood, and apply a clean, moistened wool cloth to the wound; then place another moistened wool cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and cover both wounds with double-layered drapes, securing them with all the ties according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two drapes, and use woolen cloth cut in this manner and assemble them by sewing in the groin of the breeches; one of these fastens at the base up to the back, and the other at the part near the wrist; and the other two on the shoulders, and tighten it all with the loop of the braies; and never use this cauterizing ramage with iron tools, but rather a delicate surgical knife, cut through the skin of the coions, and heat it as we have said, until the white substance that contains water is exposed; take the cautery in this manner, and pierce the syph (supposedly a type of plant or material) as before, and scrape off with this delicate hot cautery.

And the cup should be used in all ways that you can, as long as everything is clean; and ensure that the fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move carefully to avoid blood clotting and the complications of an abscess or any other thing; if anything goes against you, whether it's an abscess or a complication from blood or another issue, then treat what goes against you according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then perform the perforation as I have told you, and make sure that when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned, that the dislocation is due to moisture, place the patient in a high seat. Then, incise the abscess deeply into all the tissue, and insert the perforation along the length of the body; make the wound wide enough for all the pus to flow out. Then place cotton on top and bind it, allowing the remaining pus to drain, then treat the wound until the injury is healed. If a clean bandage does not allow the pus to escape from the wound's opening, you should insert a needle or the instrument used to drain water from dropsical patients, as mentioned before. Open the wound wider, and know that the pus will return and gather again after six months or so, and when it gathers as before, the patient's condition will improve.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hairs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme. Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say, therefore, that many abscesses occur within the hairs and even more commonly in other parts; and this is due to many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine. The one who is made of vein inflammation is known by its disposition to the painful expression of the fingers, and can do well the incision on this similarity, and on other parts; and it is what you cut the heart of the tissues, then the heat goes down, and the pain subsides in a satisfying white color, and releases the suspension from all parts of the heat.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the intestines
