de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sinew.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this condition are such: if it arises from the rupture of a sinew, or from extension in the abdominal region in the area of the angles (of the body), then the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the openings; and this rupture is either due to the sinew being cut or extended, and these two types of causes arise in many ways: through striking, jumping, shouting, lifting a heavy weight, or similar actions; and the signs when it is a rupture due to extension are that it occurs little by little over a long period, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess is evenly distributed all the way to the perimeter, because the rupture pushes the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac. aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to move the intestine back into its place within the wound if it can; then be careful on his collarbone between your hands, and ease the cheeks; then stretch the heart above, and cut all the flesh from the bones along. Then insert the fingers inside the groin according to what you need to open the wound, so that they can come out; then scrape off the healthy skin that is under the hard white flesh until all the white flesh is completely exposed on all sides. Then point your index finger towards the direction of the bone, between the white flesh that is underneath the skin of the groin, and between the second flesh, and separate what is behind the bone, and between the second flesh; then move your right hand inside the heart of the bones, and place the white flesh on top in your left hand, and ease the bone towards the lower part, and as you do this, command the assistant to stretch the bone up high, and free what is attached at the rear behind the ligament; and if there is no sign of the intestine wrapped up or hard white flesh, then insert it into the stomach underneath. Then take a needle with a thick thread made from X threads, and insert it in the rear part of the flesh after the skin of the groin; then cut the testicles that appear through the threads until there are IIII threads; then arrange them one on top of the other in a cross shape, and tie the flesh that we mentioned earlier as being underneath the skin of the bones with a strong ligature from both sides; then wrap the testicles with the thread, and tie them together so that no vessels that nourish them can enter, and no pus comes out. And place the ligature according to the first long ligature, leaving two fingers' length of the flesh that is underneath the heart of the bones free after these two ligatures; then cut off the flesh that is underneath the skin of the bones until it is smooth and curved as we mentioned before; then apply moist wool to the wound, and place the ligature that we mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never should the white skin be cauterized as we have said, after incision, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leaves the wound open as long as it needs to heal; if it takes time to close, it can be helped with hot water, and we should apply what we have said, as long as it needs; then treat the wound with another cure, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	herniated cartilage
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, one never sees anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like a root which is joined to a stem, in such a way as you would bind vessels, after cutting them slightly on the side, then open it and treat the abscess of him who operates, until the vessels stop bleeding; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur from sudden force, as we have said, and open the vessels; and let no intestines drop out as they become detached, and if they do, it is bad, and repair them every hour; nevertheless, if it persists too long at this point, it is thought to be a wound or an abscess, until the intestines drop out; and this happens due to the extension of the abscess which is located on the vessels, as it expands then becomes softened and inflated; and its cure is through cautery, as we have previously said; and never should it be treated with iron in this manner. And so, the patient should lie down on his back, between your hands, then cut the vessel of the rupture deeply according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the abscess that lies beneath the skin next to the flesh, take the razor, and place it over the visible part of the abscess; and press it firmly into the belly, then cut both visible parts of the abscess on top of the razor, and stitch them up; then remove the razor, and do not cover or extend the abscess or anything else, as I have told you regarding the cure for intestines; and treat it through wound care.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they become dirty and the wound is clean, do so.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the rupture, but cauterization on this limb is more mobile and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the thick skin of the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often, the skin of the joints becomes softened in no men, because the fluids inside are mollified, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wishes to heal it, to lay the patient on his back and cut the softened skin from the natural skin; then bring together the two edges with a stitch, and if you see, first sew the superfluity of the mollified skin with three stitches or four firmly; then cut between the stitches and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and let the thread out.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement (Double cautery)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is condemned in our law, and for that reason I would not like to speak of it in this book; nevertheless, there are two ways in which it is necessary: one is to answer knowledgeably when asked about it and the cure; and the other is because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as a goat and a sheep and a cat and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we use attraction, let the animal be seated in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then, with your hand, press them until they return to their normal state and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the operation of castration: You must tie the animal and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then bind the suspensory, and cut into each one as you've well scraped them; and leave no soft or subtle pain that is on the veins; and this method of castration is different from that which is done by attraction, because at attraction, there might be something remaining in the testicles, causing lust in the animal; then treat the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermophrodite is according to two manners of men: one is that between the two sexes opens up as the figure of nature of a woman, where he has hair, and sometimes shortens the urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, who have hair on their lower limbs as well as a phallus and two vagina-like openings.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is to bind all the loosened joints tightly and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for those whose urination jumps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the rash
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tendons are a charred tissue attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and no woman has ever had it so great as a hand, and it is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should remove the excess of tendons from your hand or fingers, and cut them gently; do not cut too deeply, lest bleeding occurs, which is the cause of many complications, while curing it with another cure until it is healed; and for another condition that arises at the mouth of the wound, and its use, and perhaps suddenly jumps out, and resembles a claw, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to take care of it, as we have said concerning the wound, and treat it until it is healthy.
de erratique	de erratique" translates to "erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of a woman is not properly understood, or when the opening is small; it is innate by birth, or accidental due to illness that arises; or it is caused by an adjustment of humors, or subtle or specific afflictions, and occurs in various parts, be it in the uterus, or on the side, or below, or wherever; and it influences conception, childbearing, and sometimes even the qualities of the offspring; and knowledge of these things comes from observing the signs of labor.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the dislocation is recent, it appears soon either on its own or through movement.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If the dislocation is delicate and recent, acting swiftly: place both index fingers together, with the woman facing you on her back, spreading her legs; then form both sides of the joint until the delicate dislocation is reduced and the joint is stable; then take wool and moisten it in oil, place it over the area, and have the woman lie on her back each day so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the dislocation is hard and complex, it is necessary to use a scalpel-like instrument resembling a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from fire, hold it with a cloth and compress it; have the medicines that stop blood, such as witch hazel, dragon's blood, incense, in abundance; then apply a large poultice so that the wound does not close; and thus do this for a long time, and then apply a dry linen bandage; and continue other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is swelling from heat, if it is not an abscessed wound, it needs to be treated in this way:
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscessed swelling in the heat, it should not be probed or punctured.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without proper treatment, can become chronic. In the previous section, we discussed the signs and symptoms, and I will now describe the treatments for them.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are in the advanced stage during pregnancy, are not easily detected, unless they require treatment with heat.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the vagina can be felt; these are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then apply pliers to tighten her, and press on her roots, then sprinkle medicine to stop blood flow, such as fennel and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And if blood continues to flow, let it subside in a decoction of sumac and apple tree bark and gall and similar things, and then take flour from barley, and mix it with honey and wax, and make a paste to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is still wet, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If no, make the patient breathe with bellows on the back and massage the breasts gently; then take lint, soak it in plantain juice or alder juice mixed with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, continue to treat the wound with a clean dressing until it is cured; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles an open sore, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	about abscesses of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the body, such as cancer and previous abscesses, and sores and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess that occurs in the body, which is not like other abscesses that are hollow; and if you see the work of fire, consider whether the abscesses are aggressive at the beginning of their appearance, full of heat and fever, and if they turn red, as you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not then hasten to pierce, but make the patient suffer until the pain is eased; then place him in a reclining position, supporting his back and drawing his legs away from each other, and gather his feet towards the side of the affected leg; spread his thighs apart, put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then suck the bag toward the patient's right side, and insert the instrument used to open the abscess, by which means the shape [of the abscess] is obtained. And it is necessary that when you insert this instrument, that you first push the handle in deeply to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters inside from the instrument does not go further than it should, and it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the bottom of the abscess with cloth, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and he should place the handle of the instrument above, and tie it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and it is incised gently by hand, if necessary cover the opening with a soft sponge; and when the bowel is emptied, put moistened oil-soaked tents into the wound, or green oil soaked in rosewater; then place the tent firmly over the wound at the full margin of the ulcer, and put on top of it clean, damp cloth soaked in alder juice or cooked mullein; then treat the patient after two days of dressing until he is healed; and never raise the ulcer or the wound with a water-and-honey enema, nor with water or cooked lily roots and long herb medicines; then return to dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the ulcer, it is necessary to avoid heating with iron, but treat it as we have said in the preceding section.
de l’enfantement	from childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Knowledge of the dance is first to understand the figure of natural childbirth, and its signs are when you see a woman in labor and she desires to breathe heavily: then haste should be made for the child to come forth; then know that these children are according to the natural figure, coming out headfirst, and seconding with them; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child comes quickly; for as it descends on its head, it seconding with him, and the mother rids herself of her superfluities through good purification; and this one who does not come in this way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes upon its feet, but goes into the body where it sticks, or into the hand, or onto the belly, or sometimes turns around by chance onto its neck, and other evil positions; so it is necessary for a skilled person to understand these things well, and defend themselves from error and deception, and I will show you all the positions, how one must help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon the head by natural cause, and the woman is giving birth painfully, and her strength is weak, she should be placed on a saddle, or women should hold her; then prepare oil of fennel or fenugreek, boil it, and then insert the small spatula between her teeth as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut through the second joint, and chop at its finger as much as the moisture which is deeply embedded; press the woman's stomach until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with fenugreek muscylee with oil of sisament; then make her cough and sneeze from a cold state, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will emerge.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are too weak, it is necessary to gently reset them little by little; and if they still cannot enter, place the woman on a seat and raise her feet up high; then remove the seat from the ground and turn off the woman so she does not want to stand; and if her hands cannot enter, and the child dies, cut through the hand at the previously mentioned joint, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the exit of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on its feet, it needs to be pushed up, and then it is slowly turned, keeping them even; then press on the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to the knees, as commanded, and is given strength, it will sneeze from the position; if it jumps further, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, if it is turned little by little, according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as we have said, take a small amount of musk, oil of roses, and gum resin, and grind them all in a mortar; then apply this mixture to the woman's body both internally and externally, leaving it for an hour after placing her in warm water up to her ribs. Then place her on a seat, make her sneeze, press her mouth and nose, and gently massage her stomach, as the child is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the emergence of the child onto its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this condition, they should slowly move their hands; then lay down on their collarbone, and let their feet hang downwards, and lie on their side; and fold their hands little by little, then take their hands and press them onto their belly, and remove the cushions from below, until it is flat downwards; if the child does not cry, they should take their feet and move them, then move their belly upwards, then turn their hands inside out; and gently rock the child; and instruct the woman to press herself while the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes out with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman rise and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her down on a bed and turn her legs up; then administer the musk (or ointment) that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, seat her on a chair, and try to bring back the hand; and deliver the child according to its natural position, make her sneeze, and command her to press as hard as possible.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its mother's chest, with its hands spread and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold his hand still, then move it little by little and gently; and when it is even, he should apply a light, muscly compress of wool and oil, as we have said, then command that it moves slightly and slowly; and once this is done, let it rest on a certain spot, and command him to press (it); and make him sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner, throughout all of this.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it proceeds in this manner throughout all the secondine (stage), if the secondine adheres to your fingernail, as long as the moisture is drained; and if it sticks to his face and neck, cut it from the corner of his mouth so that it is not held back, and let the child breathe; then turn the baby inside out, as you have placed him properly, and command the woman to press (him) once; then gently unbind.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the opening of the eyes
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never more than three or four at once; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are strange things and do not live long, they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and their destinies are decided by the will of God, who controls the womb; and they never emerge as naturally as any other child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born deformed, as we have said, and the cure is subtle, making it quickly and easily, doing what is necessary for their salvation.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They should never be formed in the womb I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child according to the measurement of its wise nature, and it is necessary that the midwife knows all this, for there may be some chance event; then she must act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has lost her child in the womb, as I have said in the previous division, and there is no sign of delivery, and you are forced to intervene manually; it is necessary that you know if the woman's health is good, and she does not suffer from fear or grief due to the loss. It is recommended that the woman be lying on her back, with her legs raised, and her bowels relaxed downward. The attendant should apply two parts of oil, or she should remain in bed so as not to be disturbed during the child's descent; then gently rub the mother's vulva with moist olive oil, mixed with althae and fenugreek powder and flaxseed. Then, anoint the midwife's hands with this mixture and these herbs. Then, place the fingers lightly inside the vagina, then pull gently on the perineum until it becomes manageable, and take care that the baby descends onto her chest; if necessary, insert the fingers into her own or her daughter's anus, or between her labia, or in her mouth, or under her tongue, or near her beard, or in the vagina, or along the sides, and if the delivery is on the ground, place a hand on her belly and between her legs; and pull gently until it becomes free. The finger should be held in one of these positions that we have mentioned, until the vaginal opening is empty. This is the shape of the perineum:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then find another joint, where you need to use it most, so that the extraction is even; and then move it equally from one side to the other to pull it out, and let the joints hold tightly, just as this shape is:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, apply no oil to its joints, but press it into that part and pull the other part; and if nothing remains, place this joint higher up on the limb and do this until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward before the other and it cannot return due to tightness, you should wrap it up with a cloth until it is entirely removed; then cut at the joint of the foot or the knee, and do the same for the other hand, holding both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and stuck in the birth canal, and it has a sharp point assembled, you should insert the spiny spatula between your fingers and move the head and extract the water; or use the instrument called "almidach", with which the shape comes out with the instruments of this chapter that follows; and in the same way, make the baby's head naturally large; then cut the bones with pliers, and if the head pops out, it is restrained by force, as long as the moisture in the worst canal has come out; and if it cannot come out, break it into pieces until you can move it; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on his feet, it is a light attraction, and the direction towards the mouth of the wound is mild.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is twisted in the stomach or in the bowels, it is necessary that you pull it with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision on the stomach or the bowels, as much as the moisture inside allows; and if another member is broken and the feces remain, press the hand down into the wound, and draw it until it reaches the mouth of the wound; then use a knife or something similar to cut and pull it out; and if the mouth of the wound has narrowed due to hot abscess that has formed, do not work on it, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and apply poultices, using soft water with soothing herbs.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the bone is on its side, and you can make it even, as we have said for a living child; and if it cannot be moved, it should be treated in parts, leaving nothing of the dislocation.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said for abscesses that come from the wound; and if bleeding occurs, it should be treated with hot compresses, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose stomach had been cut, and another doctor had treated it, and prevented further harm.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a swelling appears in the cheek, it swells up so much that it opens, and it begins to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon for treatment, and I thought for a long time, but I could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong poultice, and an egg came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed because that belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, as long as the woman was in better condition; and after the woman had lay thus for a long time, she suddenly felt some relief from her pain. I have never heard this chapter mentioned except when the master encounters something strange that he knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the woman back to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of the press, with which one binds the books; and at the turning to the two feet of the two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the opening at the top should be two fingers' width across, and the edge of the tree, one palm length and a half; and between these two pieces should be an adjustment of this same horn, firm in both directions, half a palm's length or a little more; and this adjustment is inserted into the mare's mouth to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and it should have two adjustments, as you can see, one palm length long and two fingers' width wide; and when opening the mare with all the instrument, have the woman lie down on her side, with her knees bent and legs spread, then press both adjustments into the mare's mouth together, holding the end of the instrument beneath her thighs; then open your hand over the entire instrument, as you did with the pliers, according to how much you opened the mare's mouth.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all diverse and varied, and when the skilled surgeon has arranged them in order, their use is more rapid and easier for the operator due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument even if you have not arranged it, for the necessity does not excuse the lack of preparation.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When assisting at childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath and then make her sneeze slowly; hold her hands to her mouth and nose, and if she coughs through them, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is a no, take I will, and make I an opening or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia, and centory; all these herbs, or any of them, are cooked or put in water over the fire; then place a cane or an opening through which the vapors can enter the wound, and the other end in the mouth of the wound, and hold it there until the vapors go inside the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the treatment does not help, then proceed with the next step.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not strong enough, instruct the patient to moisten their left hand with oil of turpentine or musk, then release it into nature, and seek the second sensation; and when they feel it, press and stretch it little by little straighteningly, so that the pain does not occur during extraction; but it must be moved slightly to the right and left, then released.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the pain is tightly closed, we have mentioned the cure of sneezing and herb fumes; and if it does not improve from all that we have said, be careful not to suck; but it is appropriate that he who has a tight mouth, ties it to the woman's calf, then gives her a four-part remedy enema; she will vomit it out and recover; however, if she throws up, there will be a bad smell in the stomach and head, and the patient will feel worse.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, then suitable fumigations should be used: no one among the ancients has tested the fumigation of purslane and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which the woman is fumigated to stop the flow of blood and the bleeding so is this one.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass similar to a vase, and the narrow part is placed in nature, and the wider opening over fire; and the fumigation should be on charcoal, and the herb until it is burned, and then repeat.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not had their foundation pierced, instead having a subtle mark: therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this mark with the proper instrument, and not let it be touched with a sharp object, then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, and treat it with care until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, insert a plug of wool or cloth, and leave it for several days, and when the child is strong enough to move around in rooms, then remove it.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And this sudden stopping of the wound or abscess should never occur; it is necessary to cover this stopping: if it is cured, as we have said about the stop of the pain.
de la fistule dou fondement	regarding the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that originate from below the foundation are called nodosities and are larger than those that come from above the foundation in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when this nodosity is old, it can open up, and still produce moist, white or subtle discharge, and these fistules do not heal; they are known because of the emission or discharge when the patient has defecation, and sometimes they spontaneously rupture.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they puncture the fistulas that reach into the bladder, and half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and the roots of the testicles.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus, you recognize the fistula present in the fundament, and it is not present: and it is that you insert your index finger into the fundament and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, if you insert a thin plunger or a horsehair, as long as you feel the plunger or hair in your hand; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out with extraction or venting or moving, as we have said: know that it will not perforate; be careful in treating it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urethra, if it lets go of the urine, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is cut near the hip joint, then the veins nearby are in danger; if there is no curvature or change in the pain around it, and it continues to be bent, and neither medicine nor a quick dressing helps, then there is no sure cure for these persistent fistulas other than hard work and the vain attempts of those who meddle.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is neither persistent nor ancient, there is hope for healing by fire, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on their back in your hands; they extend their legs up to their thighs, and their thighs are inclined towards their belly. Then you apply a tent of iron, or cloth if there is curvature, as long as you know where the vein is located.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain deep within, you should then press your index finger upon it; he will feel that the ache is being pierced. Either uncover or feel between your thumb and forefinger for satisfaction or a hard spot; if you find none, do not work further, as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One cannot be certain of healing anything, but this happens infrequently. The aid that can be provided is to apply hot cautery along the width of the fistula, as has been previously mentioned; fill it completely with heat until it reaches the depths of the foundation, and do this two or three times, ensuring that these charred marks, resembling a bird's feather, are thoroughly burned. Then cure the wound with moist compresses, until the charring subsides, and finally apply an ointment that is soothing and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If, however, he cannot be made healthy in any other way; and if the tent (or infection) penetrates between the bones, and does not pierce to the muscle that is at the base of it, and there is a thick covering of flesh or fat between your finger and the tent, then you will see the fistula opening through the covering towards the heart; if it is cut from the beginning of the fistula, and removed backwards before the tent, and then cauterized afterwards while it reaches the base of the tent, the tent will be delivered and healed; then beware of those evil-looking ones that resemble a bird's feather, and do not leave anything.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain strikes you, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery combines two good things: that is to say, the burning of these carefully adjusted parts, and the inflammation of blood and the dryness of moisture; then treat the wound with moist ointments or things ground in oil, as long as the bones are soft, and pull out the burned parts from inside; then cure the wound with hot compresses and hard charcoal, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because once it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears all the way to the bottom of the foundation and is removed from the body, if you press on its root or foundation, it hurts.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the pain, and it is between two things—the skin or the flesh or bones—and it is about to pierce through, if there is no other way of hope and cure, by means of one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it deeply, or if you can gently press on it and treat it as before; but be careful not to go too deep, that you do not cut the tissue holding the foundation, and cause discharge against your will; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or you remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut away from the foundation, either with a probe or another instrument; then purify the wound as best as you can; try to restore the wound and prevent the fistula from spreading beyond the foundation. If it is a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And they are never formed in this way: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it remains on one side near the base of the skin above, take a tent-shaped tool at the top according to this form.
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And push the wire crookedly inside, pushing the tent all along the fistula as far as it will go at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is deeply embedded at the base within, then pull out the wire from that perforation, thus pushing your other finger or base into place; and hold the top of the wire, bringing together both joints, holding them against each other, and leaving it for one to two days; and do not move it again until the wires have severed the tissue between them and stopped bleeding; then treat the wound while it is still fresh and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If you cannot pierce the fistula, no matter how much you try, it is not pierced deeply enough.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to make the closure too tight, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the sharp, spiky fistula that is made if it is deeply and painfully inflamed on one side and cuts into the other; but not on both sides, so as not to close it tightly or improperly, as you can see.
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the anus, like a grain of resin, with small and large ones, oozing blood, and those that protrude from the anus or its opening; they have little moisture, sometimes a bit of citrus water or blood, and have a reddish color. The treatment for hemorrhoids located within the anus is to instruct the patient to stay in bed until the anus heals completely and the children are delivered. If urgent action is needed, grasp them with pliers or your fingernail, then cut them at their roots. If they won't let go due to moisture, grab them with a piece of cloth, cotton, or a chamoix, pull them out gently, cut them off, and apply hot powder as directed in the cautery chapter; or cauterize them as described in that chapter, treating other ailments until they heal. If the anus cannot be opened, use a strong enema to wash what is inside so it can come out easily.  When the patient is relieved and the children are delivered, the treatment is light; cut off the hemorrhoids with your fingernail or pliers, then treat as previously mentioned until they heal completely, without fear of incision by metal.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary, you must administer the stitch in this manner: take the twisted thread, and wrap it around an needle, then draw the thread on top and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it is too wide, tighten the thread, then tie it off, and pull out the needle, and do thus with all the rest, leaving one end to drain the excess blood; then place a moist cloth or gauze on the wound, and cover it, and instruct the patient to rest. And then leave it until the stitches are ready, and when they have fallen, treat them with dressings and other remedies, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Carefully and thoroughly from herbs or foundations
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is a drying up of herbs in the intestine, due to constraints of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine avails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape off the skin with a spatula or your finger, without leaving it moist; then treat it as it should be while it is fresh; and if it cannot be softened, repeat the scraping stronger than before, until it becomes healthy, and is cut; then treat it while it is healed.
dou fremit	He trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A mole is a small, smooth growth under the skin that penetrates deeply; it does not hurt, and its presence is often only noticed because it can be felt, and it smells like something dead due to its tremor, affecting the entire body, especially the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane from an ostrich feather or a strong falcon feather, and place this cane on the tremor until it encircles the tremor entirely; then turn your hand over the entire cane as you remove all around the tremor, and set it in its place, pulling out the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this of an iron or steel cable according to this form, and be subtle from below and draw from above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not cut, so as to hold both, and press. And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as it is in front or at the beginning of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a dish
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never use a silver or gold enema, or melted iron or wire; and never use these small and large instruments according to those to whom they are entrusted.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	He who thus administers treatment to children and those who are weak and afflicted, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema is small and wide at the top, or the abdomen is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say there should be a constriction or the abdomen bound as you see, and the faeces inside perceived; and have on one side two openings, and on the other one; and the abdomen, whether filled with medicines from a bladder of an animal or parchment, should be pierced all around with small openings, and there should be one space between each opening, then thread through these openings one strong thread twisted in the shape of X or any other pattern, and tighten the abdomen as if it were a bow; and when the medicine is inside, attach the instrument in front with a strong thread, then perform the enema; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and moisten the wound with oil or egg white or a similar substance, then gently press it; then the helper should massage both hands together until it is completely relaxed, then remove the compress, and ease the patient's legs against the wall, and allow the medicine to escape as much as possible; if he sleeps soundly throughout the night, it will be of great help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for a stomach disorder and the medicine quickly escapes, then it returns as soon as it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the foundation, or an abscess, it should be a very delicate enema, just as for a child; and this is the shape of the delicate enema that tightens the skin.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now I will tell you about the remedies for hands and medicine according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the place where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword or knife, or lance or spear or arrow or similar objects; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the neck, or head, or side, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is caused by stone or similar objects, and the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound is deep, and you doubt an abscess forming: treat it immediately, especially if there is little blood from the wound, and have the patient drink wine and avoid heavy meats.
