Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be healed, let his flesh be reduced and let him not drink wine or eat charred food; and apply a poultice of rose oil only, or vinegar stipple; and if there is a hot abscess, apply it to the wound while it is still fresh with all its blood, and do not let the air, powder—which I will speak of later—move it, and if the fire has moved it, apply any herbs as long as they are healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as the size of a sword or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tenting, then bring them together with stitching, as I will say about abdominal wounds, from the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and deep, but only holds for a little while, then treat it with medicine, and replace the skin with hard wood, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats, such as beef, cooked wheat, chicken, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in the flesh or leather, and it does not affect the bone, but rots entirely through, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which no blood can be stopped by medicines, then cut the artery, and if you loosen it with a thread, and it still does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you place this powder which solidifies so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method of the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts fresh charcoal, mix them finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it until it spreads well throughout and adheres to all its parts; then bind it tightly and leave it undisturbed if it does not swell, for the medicine should not be removed as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should charcoal be used alone if you do not have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no such powder applied; but put on some prepared remedies, or a paste of barley flour made with water and honey, until it cools; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you below about the fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the collar (or neck).
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the collarbone and it is simple, with no distinction between it and any other part of the bone, but there is damage to the nerves or arteries in the collarbone.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy but to let them heal naturally and not apply anything restrictive, as that would harm the nerves and cause them to retract; do not put any sharp objects on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body. But use medicine, such as washing with warm water mixed with rose oil and clean bandages also in warm water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cutting it open and binding it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and severe, filled with pus and bowing, pierce them or cut them lower; if the artery is severed, and bleeding occurs, ignore it, and apply cauterization as necessary; if the pain is in the throat or heart, cut around them without touching the throat, but reset them according to their natural position. Then proceed cautiously, leaving no bandage for several days while treating with remedies until healed; if the wound has pressed into the bone, dig out any pieces of bone you can, and leave those you cannot, allowing the wound to fester and become less severe. If the wound is fresh, apply the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and deep, pay attention to the signs of pus as the patient alone can show: then know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not so deep, and fresh with all its blood, do not delay for the first hour in applying powder, nor bind it tightly until the poison has completely left and returned to the body, and freed the patient; but apply a good dressing and bind it twice a day. And if you have no dressing, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and keep the patient sleeping on the wound for three or four days (or more); if there is no spasm, nor any bad tremors or strange weakness, then know that the wound is healing.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds with various remedies and others, as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; then treat it as appropriate.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deeper on the front or back, treat it as for that which is before; if it is large, use stitches; and if it is small, use powder; and if it involves bone and has pieces, clean the wound thoroughly if they are suitable; and if they are not suitable, let the wound fester, and alight the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruption of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound, no time does the intestine or the intestines' nerve protrude outward; and stitching is more difficult, and never is a small wound better than a large one, unless the intestines are set back in place, tightly against one another. Because the intestines quickly swell, causing pain, if they are not set back firmly, and because a smaller wound necessitates moving the intestines less, therefore it is preferable to move the intestines gently back into position when dealing with a belly rupture compared to other wounds. And know that there are four types of ruptures:
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and there is no internal organ involved, and it is a difficult thing to heal, then this is one of two ways: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth with hot water alone, or cook water with juniper berries, cinnamon, and cloves, and soak the intestines until the swelling is removed; and never use this wine-based treatment, as it only makes it worse.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or other fluids, and the veins are cooked, because that makes entry easier for a little while; and if it cannot enter, they make a small incision with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is to move the veins, that we should not cut them unless absolutely necessary; and this is the instrument to split: incise within the hollow and divert it, or you will see the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound has enlarged and the intestine bursts out, if you can return it to its natural position in its proper place, do so, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and located in the lower part of the abdomen, it is necessary to make the patient lie on his back and elevate his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, place the head and testicles higher than the parts below, and also ensure that the rupture in the belly is in one of the two parts so that the damaged part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to attend to what I say regarding both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, prepare what you will use; then take in your hands a clean, warm, and moist liquid to cover the entire wound, and close the lips; this is the common method of stitching. Puncture the skin with one or more needles, according to the size of the wound, and leave two spaces at the head of the wound, and sew a strong thread through; then perforate both sides of the leather with the two parts of the needle, from the inside until you have perforated this part, and bring together the two parts of the needle; then tie a double thread around the needle from both sides, and bring together the two edges of the wound neatly, and leave two spaces, and sew another needle; then secure the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue to do so until the entire wound is held together; the needles should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, for the thin ones will penetrate all the flesh, and the too-thick ones cannot enter well. Therefore, they should be medium. Do not pull the needles too far from the flesh and leather, or else they will open the wound before sealing it; then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and place a tent or cloth at the end of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; this stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because you only need one or two stitches, and it is like sewing a garment; and I sewed a wound on a man who had been stabbed in the belly, which was gaping from a knife, and was over a palm wide, and there were intestines protruding more than two palms, and the wound was in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where none were to be found, nor any medicines; and I put clean cotton over the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and the thread from the opposite side until it reaches this one; when it has pierced through the fabric in a straight line, pull the thread on the other side until it emerges here, where you first inserted the needle, and then pierce it again from the inside to the outside, and so on until the stitching is complete. This method is similar to how a leather worker stitches fur, leaving the thread on one side and pulling it through from the other.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of stitching, which Galen calls "so-called," is like a method that joins the two parts together naturally, and one of its ends is applied to the other end in this way: take an needle with a close thread, pierce only through the skin, and leave the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle and pierce from the other side towards the inside, through both ends of the thread; then pierce each of them from the other side towards the inside, through the other threads on either side; and this is the most usual method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen calls this method "so-called," and no one testifies to it, for one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; then one needle should be inserted from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew up wounds; and know that when the opening is in the belly, the stitching is more difficult than that of other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you open the fresh wound and drain all its blood, if the flesh has moved, you should close the gaping wound and apply a dressing; then put on charred powder and, if the flesh has moved, apply any available treatment until the wound heals; cut the thread, and make sure the bandages are secure, and use myrrh; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, put a piece of old cotton and move it two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these arrangements for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound is affecting vital members, it is necessary that you apply a light linen cloth dipped in hot temper oil or rose oil around the angles and under the armpits; and if it causes pain or pus formation frequently, and especially if the pus reaches the intestines, clisterize it with black wine gently, and more so if the pus affects the larger intestines, for they heal more easily than the smaller ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal organ, called "jeun" (fasting), cannot heal when it is inflamed, and this is due to the weakness of the veins, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the nearness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the blood clot jumps out of the wound, it should be pushed back as with the intestine, while it is fresh; but if it has become old and turned white or black, you must tie up the black part to prevent further bleeding, for there are veins and arteries inside; then cut away the tissue in between, and hang the two pieces from the bottom of the wound outward until the clot falls out, thereby facilitating its extraction.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, it cannot be restored in any man, as I have seen a nobleman with a lance through his abdomen; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became infected and developed into a fistula, and there were issues with excretion and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to try subtle remedies until he was healed, and the wound was sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his stomach; but he felt no pain, only improved conditions, and food and drink; and certain experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be treated in this manner: take a large needle, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the needle has gone through the opening, place it between the two lips, so that it draws the mouth together; then cut off the head of the needle, and let it remain so that it cannot be opened; then insert another needle in the same way until the wound is completely closed; and heal the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That which is most acute in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and can be tied with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine, in this way: take the tip of this intestinal thread, very stripped, and then tie it to the tip of this thin linen thread twisted, then wind the thread onto the needle, and sew up the intestine, and arrange it in the rupture; and this method of sewing is not stronger than according to reason and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, no one can heal it with any subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or whether it is a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	You know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula," especially when it is covered with hair and deeply seated.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is, according to medical truth, hard and white, causing no pain, and just like the feathers of a bird; it never heals clearly open, sometimes thin and other times thick; sometimes soft, other times firm; and as I have spoken about in the division of wounds, every wound that does not heal, and there is no pus, is due to one of nine causes: namely, the excess of blood or abscess; its evil nature; because there is hard material inside, preventing it from healing; excessive bowing; bad quality flesh; improper medicine; because the corruption is in a state similar to plague; because of the region's inherent delay in digestion and the slow arrival of health; or because of bones or veins. I have already explained all these causes, their signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body, for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, or the small intestine, bladder, any rib, or the spine, and any joint of the hands or feet. If they affect the main part of a limb and its similar structures.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal and require hard work and knowledge. If there is a fistula that does not come to the surface as I have described, but you are confident in its cure, take a needle or iron, if the fistula is straight; and if it is crooked, seek a subtle pliers, for the pliers bend around the curvature. And if the fistula has an opening through which you cannot easily insert a probe, rinse it with one of the openings, because moisture flows from one opening to another and cleanses it; then hold it firmly in your power so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and whether it is well-formed, and ask the patient in pain where he feels it and what part. And when you know exactly where it is, and whether it is distant from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or any of the openings I have mentioned, then cut it as I have told you, and remove the bad tissue and the corrupt flesh within; and then cure it as best as you can, and insert moist medicated plasters until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom. And then place hot poultices over it while it is healthy; and if, after this, it is not healed, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the primary limbs, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is decay and blackening, then the king must treat it for as long as the decay persists, until it is healed; and if it is not healed and remains bowed as before, know that you are not yet allowed to go further: expose and cleanse it as much as possible, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If no, know that the decay is too severe, and there is nothing to be done; if there is no other way but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can extract it with pliers suitable for such a task, and if there are many bones, break them one by one, leaving none behind; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cauterize and dry, and relieve the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something corruptible on the wound, and let it fester around the bones, and then they will become more easily healed; and if it is a large bone, like the leg or thigh, scrape off the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then close the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption that extends almost to the bone, cover it completely until the corruption is gone, then treat it as long as it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you can take an example from it and provide aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that arose inside his body, causing matter to accumulate in the leg, and he suffered from a large abscess for which there was no opening; but they worked so excessively over it that the abscess opened, and many things corroded, becoming a fistula, and causing many openings through which everything leaked bowels and moisture from the body. Many tried to cure him for two years, without any wise man in the art of healing, until I was called to see his leg and the remedies used, and what was corrupt through the openings affecting great parts of the body; and the skin of the young man turned red, and took a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and I found that some came together against each other in every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then quickly grabbed a tool and inserted it into one of the gaps until I discovered part of the bone, which I found corrupted and broken, with the corruption reaching down to the bone itself; I understood what appeared to be the bone's corruption, and believed that there was no other corruption except the one I had left; and I began to treat the wound with many different medicines for a long time, but it would not heal. Then I re-examined it and discovered the bone as it was before, and found that the corruption continued within the bone, so I treated it and then set it back in place, and focused on binding the joint; but I could only manage to insert a palm-width of the bone, and bring it back to its original state. Then I treated it with more medicines, and it healed completely and was bound firmly, without desiring to repeat the operation except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the evacuation of blood, it often becomes completely healed, and a hard callus forms in its place, and is of good disposition and causes no harm or pain at all, neither going away nor coming back.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be handled as follows: take a string and stretch it across the opening of the bone, and instruct anyone to pull it upward; then tie another thicker woolen string over the first one, and bind it to the flesh that is now separated from the bone, pulling the bone back until you remove the corrupted flesh; expose the bone where it was previously attached, and place a hot coal or a board underneath the bone to protect the flesh; and be as gentle as possible when handling the corruption, and do this at intervals.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then expose the whole flesh; afterwards, place charcoal inside, and then sew from one part to the other over the corruption; do this until it heals entirely as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and sew the bone from another part; and if the corruption is in the connection of two joints, there is no other way but to cut it off. And if the corrosion is in the thumb or the big toe, this matter is very difficult, but you must examine how the corruption opens, and cleanse it in every manner that does not harm the vein or nerve; and know that many instruments are needed to cut these bones, according to their location, appearance, thickness, size, and hardness; and for this reason, each operation requires a specific instrument; and know that practice will show you the instrument you need, according to your knowledge of this art and the signs of the diseases; choose the instrument according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint dislocates either internally or externally; and when you have treated the inflammation with medicines, but they are ineffective, it is necessary to cover that limb until the inflammation goes away, so that the patient escapes from death or evil, which is greater, due to the dysfunction of the limb; and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and then becomes pale again, since these inflammations spread from one part of the body to another. Therefore, hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of some poisonous animal, such as a sea scorpion or snake or similar, treat the inflammation at the head of the affected limb and do not allow any space for it to come back.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it extends to the hand, so that the bone is caught in the joint, preventing corrosion from reaching the arm; and if it affects the arm, it cuts through the shoulder; and if it passes beyond the shoulder, it's death, and there is no cure outside of its quantity of strength; and thus it acts whenever corrosion appears on a limb: if it starts at the first joint, it cuts after the other joints; and if it begins on the foot, it cuts through the entire foot; and if it ascends the leg, it cuts at the knee joint; and if it rises above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or binding the limb is as follows: you tie it from above and below, and stretch one assistant with each rope, and they separate the flesh that lies between the two ropes with a large spatula, until the bone is exposed, then cut or bind it, and place a piece of linen on each side so that the linen does not touch the healthy tissue, causing further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bloodletting occurs when you operate, cauterize the wound carefully or apply powders to restrain it; then return to your treatment until it is complete, bind the affected limb securely with a suitable bandage, and tend to it until it heals; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in great pain: he had a blotch that seemed like a burn from fire, and that ulceration began on his right lower leg, spreading over the entire leg. When the man saw the ulcer, he covered his leg, and it healed. But a long time later, the ulcer returned on his left hand, and he came to me, and I put protective things over the wound after purification, but it would not stop. He asked me to cut off his hand, and I refused, as I had hope of repulsing the matter; I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, since the man's strength was weak. He became completely desperate, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it healed; and I have heard no other story like this, unless it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess should form in a fleshy part, and remain for so long that it causes great pain; then it bursts and pierces the flesh, and remains in the muscles as though a vessel; and the skin above is as delicate as fine cloth, and does not go all the way to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called 'sain' (not a fistula); but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, it is called a 'fistula'; and the flesh should be cut away all around, especially when it is delicate like fine cloth; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the flesh opens and the corruption is not completely healed, and the flesh is thick, cure it with a enema in this way: examine if the swelling is great and if the bowel that results has a bad smell; then prepare an enema of Egyptian medicine thus: take equal parts of alum, oil, litargire (arsenic sulfide), and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey. Then take as much as you need and mix it with water and honey, and pour this into the swollen area to clean it; leave the medicine for two hours, then drain it out, straining it; do this many times until the swelling disappears and the pus is drawn out. Do not enema with water of ashes when this medicine is not available; instead, prepare a mixture by burning vine wood ashes and pouring water over them, then strain it; enema with this until you are sure that the swelling has disappeared. If the patient cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, enema him with honey and wine or with just honey, knowing that honey has cleansing properties and that wine causes pus to drain; once done, if the swelling is well cleansed, enema with a mixture of resin as it forms, and add rose oil and wine; or use any other medicine and ointment whose properties have been discussed in the section on ointments. If the opening in the breast is small and the tube from the enema cannot enter, widen it slightly with a hot iron, and apply an ointment of Egyptian origin (basilic) until it is wide enough; if the wound is too large, cut it out as far as possible, leaving only what the enema tube can reach, especially if the opening points downward.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not allow itself to be distended; and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you see fit, prepare it in such a way that the bowel moves down to its lowest point, for when the bowel is perfect, it will not allow itself to be distended. And do not leave any part of the bowel protruding; take consolidative medicines to place over the wound, and cover it with a linen cloth that covers the entire wound. Then, as strongly as possible, close the opening in the side of the anus a little wider than before; apply soothing medication on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place this over the opening in the bowel to ease the pressure. Do not remove the large linen cloth outside for several days; those who are placed over the opening of the anus often need to be opened to release the bowel, and you must know what comes from the bowel: whether it is poison or a little or enough, or digested or undigested. Be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and how far your medicine has spread; if you see that the wound on the opening of the bowel has already healed and become cleaner, then know that health is approaching. And then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth and renew the medication.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast is bent downward due to indigestion after many days, knowing that the breast will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons manifest after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose tardy healings cause them to speak ill of their wounds, and others who do the contrary; and if the breast becomes bent downward after many days of pain, knowing that it will not open; and if it remains closed for a long time, far away from healing, then use moist medicines with substances that are beneficial in nature, as final remedies, for there is a great part of vitriol, which is the last medicine; take the final remedy, and apply it with rose oil, and mix it with old wine equally in substance; then conserve it and use it; and this same thing is done with cooked honey thickened, when the final remedy is not present, or you take mirra, aloes, and incense, and grind them, and make a powder on the honey while it is still warm; and then spread it on a cloth, and apply it to the breast, and never administer in large doses or roots of licorice, which is as flour and lint; and use simple or composite remedies: grind them and make a powder, and add it to the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the healing takes time, and this cure does not help, then know that corruption has penetrated fully, and exerts pressure on the bones, or the hard members, or the ligaments; as we have said about the treatment of fistulas.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A nail abscess is an infection that arises from the nail bed of the hand, or foot, or occasionally in other areas; and when it becomes old and one does not take care, it can lead to a severe abscess that oozes and runs with pus as it infects the root of the nail, and sometimes even destroys the entire nail. It causes intense, putrid pain, and the affected area swells, becoming red and large in size.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If, as we have mentioned in the previous discussion, you treat it but the treatment is ineffective, then you must remove any excess debris from under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is clean; if the nail catches fire in the char, and begins to point, and becomes blistered, then you must place the edge of the nail under the char, and pull it up, and carefully and gently cut off the char, and apply hot and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and remove it, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see both bones corrupted, treat them as mentioned above, then cure them until they are healed; and if they are fused together, and blistered, and cause great pain, then you must heal them first; then cut the nail with a sharp instrument at an angle from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the char beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain should be so severe as to paralyze the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born without hands, or has them extremely fleshy, and perhaps has part of his bones missing, and never any fingers, and none are born in the root of the joint—in such cases, birth must take place elsewhere.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born without any joints of the hand cannot move them, and he who is born with joints may not be able to move them; the size of one who is excessively fleshy should be considered in this way: cut off his fingers at their root with a wide knife.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: if you hold it tightly.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born with or develops a deformity, it is necessary that you first hold the joint firmly up to the bone, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and finally treat it as long as it remains healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come at will affect the entire body, either from birth, or from wound healing, or from a burn by fire, or similar conditions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you need to handle that wound, so it must be healed according to their natural forms; then place between two moistened cloths or sheets of linen soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or you place between two pieces of fine cloth, as long as the limbs are bound, as it should.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs at any of its joints with the palm, handle that wound as appropriate.
des vils	Des vils" translates to "from the
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These veins are thickly wrapped, full of melancholic surplus, which comes to many members of the body; and it is more present in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purging of the bowels, and then clean the wound in the temple.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of fire is according to two methods: one is with the use of cups, and drawing out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is made according to this method: first, raise the affected leg with hot water, until the flesh becomes numb, then stretch the malnourished leg from above the ankle to below the knee; then cut the vein in one or two or three places with a broad knife, then press and drain the black blood in your hand from one end to the other, as much as the sick person can endure, and then tie it, and order him to eat foods producing dark, black feces; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	They should raise the leg of the sick person, if there are many hairs, then immerse it in hot water and raise the affected leg with warm water until it turns red and swells; and if you have no bath, heat it over a fire and then compress it against the vein at the top of the thigh or near the ankle joint; then cut the skin at the point where the vein appears, and slice it from both sides until it is exposed; and it will appear red and black, and when it enters under the skin, it seems like a white cord; then pull the leg towards the foot as much as possible while it is being raised from the skin, and compress it gently at the joint, then repeat this process with another hook, just as you did before; then cut another piece if needed, and raise and compress it, and cut the vein on the opposite side; then extract it from one size to the next until it comes out completely, and cut it; and if you cannot pull and extract it, insert a needle through the entire thread and tie and pull it, and press down with your finger towards the foot, and move your hand back and forth, until it comes out; be careful not to cut it, because if it is cut, you will not be able to pull or extract it, and this will cause harm to the patient; once all of it has been extracted, place a soft, moist cloth over the wound, soaked in wine and rosin oil, and dress it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if it (the dislocation) is tight and twisted and wrapped up together, and it is not at all straight, as we have said, then you must force it in a twisted manner, but do not cover it; treat it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape to use in order to reduce a dislocated bone, if it is curved and does not cut through, until it reaches the vein; it is of great curvature, because if it were thin, it would cut through the vein, but since it must be thick as we have said, this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the main vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in hot regions where no herbs or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; it may occur elsewhere on the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that arises from below the skin, as it comes from within the body, winding and entwined between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great swelling in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude strongly, as if it were a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap a piece of cloth around it from one and a half to two inches wide, and leave it on the leg; and at all times when it does not completely come out, if you rewrap it around the cloth, and also around the new growth, and do not cover its base, as long as it is still coming out; for if you cut it, it will return to the flesh and cause abscesses and putrefaction in that place, and a grave illness. For this reason, it is necessary to treat it little by little until it is completely gone, and leave nothing in the body; and sometimes this vein is as long as five palms, or even more, and when you cut it, it leaves a raised or depressed scar, and completely comes out. And you should empty the matter inside, and apply medicine that fights putrefaction every day until the wound is healed, just like with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never again touch this vein, especially when it opens at the ankle or foot joints, and a lot of bleeding occurs; treat it then as we have said above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between leather and bone.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between leather and bone. It spreads throughout the body, moving from one member to another, causing great pain as it grows and moves until it breaks through the skin or muscle, then it digs deeper; and it breeds corruption of certain humors, just like worms, serpents, lice, and tapeworms do in the belly; and its malice is uncertain, for when it spreads throughout the body, it rises to the head, reaches the eyes, and sometimes recedes, damaging them; this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn, one cannot do so until the hair grows: therefore, you must lie the limb above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut and draw it strongly, and if the hair is embedded in the flesh, cauterize it with fire until it heals; and the greater harm it causes, the more oil it will discharge, as we have said. And if you see the hair growing near the oil, tighten the bandage below the eyebrow, then cut and draw it strongly; and it is necessary for the patient to use purification and treatment with corrective medicines to remove corrupt humors, and to wash with foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to no specific member, but rather spreads from one member to another; and I have seen this as I told you.
