Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and after that, I noticed something moving up the shoulder like a worm, as lively as live silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that limb, and moved to the shoulder, and then, shortly after, spread throughout the body, reaching the other arm; then she told me that she felt it returning around the body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled much at how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had always wanted to know if the pain would move from one place to another, but I hadn't seen it that way before, as I observed in the woman; and I thought it was because she had a dry body, her veins exposed, and this constrained breathlessness appeared; and I did not find these things to be true for those who are healthy, with moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease heal, and the patient feels this pain as we have said, if it opens from above and below vigorously, then press until this constrained breathlessness at the site subsides; and cauterize the site; and if you do not see improvement on your own, seek help from those who expel the breathlessness, like foul-smelling pills, or serpine pills, or similar remedies.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary, according to their appearance and the part of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in the fact that there are those with sharp, small, or serrated points; some have two edges, others have lengths, and some have barbs; and they pierce different parts in various ways: into vital members like the brain, body, liver, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes out in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you below, appears: it is necessary that you struggle with the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various ways; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not fully extracted, take it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow comes out and pierces the bone, and there is pain above the brain, blackness and dimness and writhing and redness all alone, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it comes out from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses his speech and voice; and there also appear white moist pus from the wound, as if from a foul ulcer, and there is also sudden weakness like that of a horse. And if these signs appear to you, take immediate action, and extract the arrow even if it is not fully embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a wound when it breaks open or oozes, is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in hard but not empty matter; and by chance, the wound may also stop moving like the pulse, and turn black with blood, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: therefore know without doubt that death draws near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never improves is that foam without pain flows from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's skin turns pale, and they breathe heavily and stop moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow comes out in the deepest part of the flesh, it leaves small bones broken; and causes great pain and heavy breathing and deep sighing; and all the movements of the shoulder blades are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat may fall out.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the abdomen, and there is no sign of recovery through the intestines, then there is little hope for treatment or in removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, causing urine to flow out in bursts and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs—as they feel and are affected by pain and swelling in the throat, shoulder, and back; as well as in the joints and legs—are safe according to various arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, for this reason, you should do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There came to me at home an arrow that pierced the ear or the cheek: I tried it, and pulled it from the other side through the fat of the ear, and it was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in another case, an arrow pierced the fat under the skin but did not reach the paper beneath, and the arrowhead remained in the flesh towards the bone, and it was a large arrow with a blue arc, without causing any pain; the wound healed, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an Arabic arrow with ears: I cut the barbs, and pulled as much as I could, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man, which had struck his gut, and thought he was dying; but after thirty days, he showed no change in condition; so I cut the arrow, cleaned it, and pulled it out, without any ill effect.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If you wish to help a man who has an arrow struck in his back or chest, and the wound is deep; and the arrow remains stuck inside him, and he shows no change in his natural condition, nor does he experience any harm from his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man to whom an arrow struck his face and the wound became deep; he remained in great pain without relief; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I pulled out an arrow from the body of a prince, the king, which had struck him in the neck and was slightly inclined to the right side; the arrow was completely removed after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very deep.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it very gently and felt nothing; however, he experienced a sharp sensation and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I applied a soothing poultice to the joint because the swelling did not subside; and I saw the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on for several days, and thereby healed the wound; thus, the patient endured the pain for a long time until he felt the arrowhead inside his body; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it healed and I felt the arrowhead stuck in the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound with that medicine until the arrowhead became visible; and after approximately four months, the wound opened up so much that I could insert tongs, moving them from side to side, but I couldn't remove it; then I continued trying subtle and ingenious tools, until one day, as the shape appeared at the end of this chapter, I pulled on it, and I healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they consider that the nose cartilage cannot be restored: I nevertheless restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you put your trust in what I say, as books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare well little by little, and upon what is present and failing, finding new works and new tools for the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the members except in two ways: either through the vein they enter or from another side; and those that come out by the side where they entered are arrows that have left their flesh, and will never exit again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not now rise, let it grow until the flesh around it becomes rotten and relaxed; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it stay that way for several days, and each day move it a little; and then it will rise, and if it does not, pierce through everything with a thin saw, until the bone around it becomes wider, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the base of the skull and reaches one of the cavities in the brain, and none of the accidents I mentioned affect the patient: do not pull it out, but let it stay as long as it remains even after several days, for if the arrow goes further, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily and remains in the patient without any further harm, as long as the skill of pulling it out allows.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply heat as I have told you; then treat the bone while it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is withdrawn into the bone so deeply that it cannot be seen, and you aim at all your strength; and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot withdraw it because of the narrowness of the wound or because the arrow goes too deep, into a place where there are no bones, muscles, or nerves, then leave it until the wound is large enough; and if possible, pull out the arrow, and if there are any parts of the arrow that remain stuck in the bone, break off the part that holds it, and then bend or twist the remaining part of the arrow as you can, until you can withdraw it. Be careful not to damage the arrow too much while pulling it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, pull it until the joint around it becomes loose, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the symptoms of blood poisoning contradict what we have said about treatment in that chapter, then administer as we have advised; and be careful with incision on nerves and veins, and use every device you can to extract the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do this, then put him as the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it opens something within, causing the skin to swell in that place as one can see or feel: then cut above, until the pliers can grasp it, and then extract it: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, widening the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it for now and then try to extract it again until it comes out; and if there is a shaft left in the wound, press it firmly, so that the tip of the arrow enters the channel of the instrument, and then push it out, and if the arrow has been extracted from the wound, insert the instrument with its tip entering together, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clear all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow comes out in the side or the belly or the bladder or near a rib, and you can reach it, take care to remove it; avoid touching the vein and nerve, then extract it, and afterwards clean the wound, as is necessary, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles an eagle's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape [of the arrowhead] pointing downward is like the feather of a bird, to drive to the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of claws for driving and gripping, if this is the case:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	From veins from which one draws blood there are XXXI, of which there is chief XVI: namely, two jugulars behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries appearing in the temples; and the two veins in the arms of the highest, called "aspires"; and the vein between the eyebrows; and the vein at the root of the nose; and the two gales on the collarbone; and the two veins above the lips, which are called "augeherich"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly drawn from each arm are five: one is the cephalic, located on the left side and called by the common people "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and is called by the common people "vein of the body"; and the basilic is on the right side and is called by the common people "vein of the stomach", and it is located above the flexor, and is the one from which blood is drawn, opening clearly into the vein.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the healing is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains; and in the leg there are three veins: one is below the knee on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side; and the third vein, called 'nasse', is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The health of veins behind the ears aids in the cure of old catarrhs and migraines; and the quality of the healer, as I have said, is to raise the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth; then tightly twist the patient's collar around their neck until the two veins behind the ears open in two parts hanging from the head: hold them there, and where you feel the pulse below your hand, it signifies success; then take the lance, and insert it beneath the vein, all the way to the bone, then gently press your hand along the entire vein upwards, cut and sever the flesh and vein well above the bone, and let out the blood until you see; then drain and bind it until it heals; and I have already discussed incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, with an ancient and smooth migraine, and a habitual blindness of the eyes, and the flow of hot tears at their roots; and his healing quality is as I say: and it is that the patient squeezes his neck, until both arteries open widely; he feels the pulse below his little finger, and then signs with his hand; then lightly presses the heart on the artery above his little finger index, and withdraws the lancet below, and releases the artery above, and the vein, as you did with the other arteries, and lets the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and place your finger on the artery for an hour, then put cotton; then form a bandage and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their healing and extraction, as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The surgeon of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the surgeon of the skull for ancient facial diseases and migraines and redness; and its quality is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "excavator", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, allowing the blood to flow according to its quantity; then free the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy without any wide cut.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flames should not be too strong; and the healthy part should be crossed, because the bone is close, and by chance, the flame may break when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The holy water of the two veins located in the arms is useful for healing:  at the wound, at the cut, at the burn, and at facial diseases; and the quality of its holiness lies in the fact that the patient extracts his pain by twisting none of its ties, as before. Then cleanse, and make the holy water flow, both slightly narrow and long from the flame, for there is no other way.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then draw out blood with a needle, as much as necessary, and then bind it tightly on cotton.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein doctor should judge if the wound is valuable for bloodletting or requires immediate closure, and treat conditions of the face such as migraine and redness. He should pull the patient's collar tightly, strain his neck to his left hand, take a long thin flame, insert it between the nostrils where the space is, because the vein will not open properly on its own, and now the blood will begin to flow. Do not let it go too deep, and let the blood out according to necessity, then bind it for a night, as it will soon heal; this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The treatment of the two glands helps to reduce inflammation and begin healing, and is useful for many conditions such as fever, leprosy, petrifying, burning, herpes, and boils. The doctor should tighten the patient's collar around both shoulders as we have mentioned; he must be master over the patient's head, and the patient should sit on a seat. Then he should open the vein with a long cut, applying blood-letting according to necessity, then treat it with warm blood, or as required. He should repeat this process in the other veins, then unbind them, gently tightening the veins until the wound is healed, and leave it until morning so that the wound can heal.
de la sainie des leivres	from the healing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the veins in the lips above helps to open the mouth, and aids in the cure of gum corruption, lip cracks, and pain and swelling around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the healing is such that you make the patient sit before you, holding his jaw as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and you know them by their black color and the small veins around them: so cut both, and if you do not know them or are in doubt, cut the thicker one from each side, and also do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cleansing of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The cleansing of the tongue is most beneficial after the purification of the head, and it helps with conditions in the throat, and eye diseases, and mouth ailments; and the quality of the cleanser is such that the patient should squeeze it between their hands towards the sun, and gently pull out the tongue, and inspect each side for a dark vein: then cleanse both, but do not press too hard, for they are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly cleansed are done in two ways: either by pricking all the inflamed spots with a sharp object, or using a fine olive oil-soaked cloth, which is called "anesil"; and they are wide or narrow depending on the size and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	It takes on the form of a bright flame if it is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it requires skill to open veins that have a great amount of visible clotted blood, and which contain much blood clot and turmoil; and it appears in the form of an olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and is for healing the delicate veins where there is subtle citron-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is beneficial for diseases that affect the throat, and neck, and chest, and belly; and it is important for the healer to heal gently, and wash away the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it touches the artery, and blood loss occurs, then it should be stopped as I have said; and the flame should not be painful but cutting like iron.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you tighten it and choose another one; or if you desire any part of it, heal in place of it the vein between the arm, opening it clearly; and cut it with iron flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you learn the place of the vein, then it is necessary to pull the arm as you know the pulse; then mark the place with a sign and tie the arm, and cut the vein with iron flame; and be careful not to hurt the artery when you see it inflated, for that is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding at the top as urine from a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that this is a sign of an artery: then hurry and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when the vein stops pulsating, which often happens; let the arm be still, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the vein stops pulsating and dies, and there is no remedy at hand, and the artery opens up because of its own strength; then stop the bleeding by pressing on it.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of the fig tree, and cut it, and take one half of it and bind it tightly to the other side; if it remains unstained, that is good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stain blood; the staining is not too grievous in small wounds, and does not weaken the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	If the vein is infected in its upper part and lower part, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins as we have said, then the healer should wash for the nerve that is below, and if he does not reach it completely, and he cuts the nerve, it swells and the health is harmed, and perhaps it cannot heal; this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person because of its subtlety, then it is necessary to use a clean instrument to heal it, and avoid the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two bones, make it open wide.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for the head (cephalique) is beneficial, as it draws blood from the head and helps the veins; and it is good to apply olive flame or myrtle flame, for these are the safest of all veins, as they do not contain any nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is better to seek the lighter (less traumatic) method, and do not be concerned if it does not work the first time, simply try again; sometimes, the veins may swell up in certain individuals upon the first attempt, but this is nothing to worry about.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound healing is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that healing is only facilitated by maintaining health and preventing future illnesses; and one should heal in one of the three veins: namely, the cephalic, the femoral, or the basilic vein; and it is necessary to begin healing at the start of prayer, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one should heal on the first day or the third, after two or three hours on the second day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healing that is administered for illnesses has no specific time frame, but as needed each day or according to nutrition, at all hours and in all seasons; and one should not heal children until they are twelve years old, nor women who have given birth until after four weeks, up to seven weeks.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not consider the old people who have passed sixty years as healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be healed, in any way whatsoever, it is necessary that he purges the intestines with a light enema, if he has much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw the superfluous and harmful residues from the primary members; nor should one consider himself healed who is excessively salted with meat, or green, as long as it lasts, or who is gouty; and wash yourself after colic, vomiting, abdominal distress, frequent intercourse with women, heavy work, staying up late, and excessive drinking, and all things that diminish vitality, whether from weapons or the body itself; then subtilize the humors, if they are thick, through diet, drink, and medicines, if you have reason to do so; then go into a bath, if nothing hinders it, to purge blood, and heal the vein after the third day, as we have said; and beware on that day of work, trouble, luxury, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and consider yourself healthier than those whom you healed, and rub the arm twice or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct itself; and then rub the vein with your hand until the veins swell and feel them; then moisten the dressing with a little old oil, and place your left hand's finger on the vein below the bandage where you wish to heal, so that the vein does not burst and injure.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like strings in the body, and if they are afflicted with inflammation, when flame is applied, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, thus making one of these cases; and if the vein is opened, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the physicians must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, it must be attempted again and again from below or above, as long as the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen and the patient fears, let it be for one or two days without binding; perhaps it will form an abscess. Do not immerse it in water; then, resume the treatment as she prefers, and if the wound is small, open it gently and carefully, so as to not increase the inflammation; this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein engorged, do not immediately reopen it, but apply a little oil to it, because oil lightens the body of blood, and the oil binds to the vein as it flows; and so administer oil in every wound that you treat veins, to stop the flow of blood; and it has the same effect and healing power when applied to the dislocated joint. The oil becomes subtile and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs, which happens frequently, especially when the vein is only opened once and the flow of blood is small, hurry and apply a moist sponge with hot wool and hold it for an hour; this should be done after the blood stops flowing from the vein, and if it remains in place for several days without turning black or green, it will not cause harm. And if you see, apply any aloe or myrrh mixed with calament juice, or similar substances.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appear on the holy basil: then place your hand upon it, and if you feel the joint tender under the pressure of your hand, that is the sign of the evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be careful not to apply anything we have mentioned, for it may dry up without reaching the artery; but make a poultice of dry materials to harden the joint, and then use other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each pain according to its quantity and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is infected, let it drain until it turns red; and if you see a bump, leave it until it becomes smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is strong and robust, and has the skill to extract blood, to make a wider wound, with broader incisions; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, making smaller cuts more frequently, and always cutting across, not straight down; this method of dressing saves the patient from infection and nerve damage, and is better than long or deep cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body inclines towards sickness, it is necessary to give a moist drink of pomegranate juice; if he is overheated, he should take three or four incisions of bloodletting. And if he has a cold complexion, he should consume before the sickness a moist drink of mused syrup, or syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and fennel, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the sight of blood after drawing much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a broth of horse, and a subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the previous section or chapter on fainting for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to straighten his arm and heal it better later, if it is weakened by much bleeding, he should treat it gently and gradually, according to the amount of its continuous power.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to straighten his arm after the first dressing and has a strong bruise, he should heal it for seven hours after the first dressing or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to be healed from another side should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood inside the body that is already heated and causes fever; it is necessary to extract a large amount of it and widen the wound until it stops bleeding; then you must consider all the conditions for healing, and place your hand on his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come instead of healing, which happens often when the healers are careless; and you should never, when you see the arm loose and blood coming out again, and the wound is closed, press it forcefully; nor if it is bent, should you make him extend his arm painfully, for that would be bad; but leave it until he heals a second time; or if there is a point of flame, keep pressing on it until the blood congelates in the vein and put a little string soaked in water on it, then press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to drain the blood a second time, do so either in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein in the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is such that the patient bends his hand in hot water until the veins turn red; then bind it gently so that the vein appears well, and now saine through the palm, not too wide or too long; make the perforation wide, and sain the joint of the hand, and if the blood does not stop, return the hand to hot water and let the blood flow in the water until enough has been drawn. If this is the case, do not bend the hand back into hot water because it will be placed under more strain than necessary; the vein in this hand is healthier than any other, whether artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cure for the salvation of the hand's health, especially in the right hand, is effective against all painful diseases: stretch the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein is inflated; if the pain crosses over, and you feel it throughout, then nothing is amiss; but do not press too hard, as the nerve fibers are entirely naked without flesh, and then return the hand to hot water, for if the coldness penetrates into the wound, it will not heal, and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then apply oil and string to seal the wound firmly, and thus do for each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sick person should hold the remedy in their left hand to treat the mouse disease, and do it just as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The remedy for the spleen is effective against all diseases that affect the body, such as diseases of the uterus, retention of fluids, illnesses of the kidneys, and old diseases of the joints and legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its remedy is that the patient drinks hot water and rubs the vein until it disappears, binding it over the joint of the foot; and the vein goes from the ankle up to the toe, or even wider at the ankle or on the foot, which moves most effectively.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it on the foot, take care to protect the nerves that are underneath, and clean the wound as if you were sewing; and the flame should be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound will not heal, immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to drain completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound needs to be cleaned again for the first time, gently repeat it a second time on top of the previous one, as the flesh is sensitive; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and follow the same procedure with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the foot's joint, and its purification causes pain in the back when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its purification is that the patient feels relief in the bath, and by twisting four times above the ankle, otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, apply all means to clean it, for the lion is safe, and it is much relieved by manual manipulation.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you cannot twist it, let no rain of the opened vein fall on your foot or towards the little toe, and be careful with your movements; and make as much correction with the blood as you can, then loosen the bandage, place cotton on it, and tighten it; now it is purified.
des sainies de ventouse	From the suction of the cupping glass.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or iron, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: either by striking and attracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This non-invasive cupping is performed in two ways: either at full heat or without heat; and the cupping which involves pricking and extracting blood is done in twelve positions on the body, with some on the top of the head, others across the nape of the neck, and two on each shoulder, one under the chin, and two on each leg, two on each ankle, and two on each wrist. It does not involve puncturing any major veins; it only targets small capillaries spread throughout the body, which is why it does not weaken anyone, as is done with vein-sucking; and it should not be performed without due care, neither at full heat nor without heat, in any condition resulting from repletion, until all parts of the body are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness or custom, it is necessary to let the air in at each hour, at the beginning and end of the month, and every day; for there are such who, when they need to let the air in, have a heavy head; and some experience swelling and redness on their face, head, neck, and darkening as well; and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, their tongue is swollen, and they bleed; and there are such who dream, see red, feel pain, and suffer similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order letting the air in after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The physician of the muskle is helped by nature in the pain of the head ... that comes from time to time, and it is not advisable after the evacuation of all the body; this ventilation is for the health of the brain, and it is not advisable for those with a cold complexion, or scabs, as they do great harm; therefore it is not advisable for old people to use it, nor those who have cold head ailments.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is cured often becomes obtuse, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cup a little lower in doubt of obstruction.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is for the health of the head and the brain, and therefore it is useful for straining of the eyes, and splitting of the channel of the sperm, and all obstructions; but it should be applied gently, as if it is too tight, it can cause obstruction to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The symptoms as the costals joints are filled with pain, and eye pain, and migraine, and strangling, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it's in the blood flow of the basilic; and you must instruct the patient to press his hand gently so he does not cut the artery, and let no bleeding occur.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The symptoms under the chin indicate a disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases in the mouth; and it's related to the blood flow in both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The symptoms in the shoulders indicate a disease that arises from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The drainings of cuts are as valuable as three veins in the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the healthy person not to cut too deeply, for the flesh is devoid of fat, and knows how to separate veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventose (suction cup) on the croup is as valuable as hemorhoids from the depths, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the ventose be large and made of iron, so that it draws well; but if it is too delicate, it may break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses on the legs close tightly because they draw blood from all over the body, and they are as valuable as ancient pains in the kidneys, bladder, and intestines, and they open up obstructions; and are located at the two thighs, two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring about various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a cup (ventouse) is as follows: you apply it at first without suction, then gently create suction and hold it firmly, moving it evenly, until you see the skin turn red and blistered, and open the wound's channels; then remove it and be mindful of the condition of the skin, for some have very sensitive or porous skin. It is only necessary to strike once, making the wounds wide and deep; apply suction gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is deep, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to open the channel of the deep wound.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very sharp, it is necessary to strike the third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice once only.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must often strike; and if the pain is sharp, we must persevere until the veins are pierced suddenly. It is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and calloused hands, to apply oil to the suction cups: it can be violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it's in ivy, watercress oil, or lotus oil, or chamomile oil, or any similar herb.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amber oil, or balsam, or donkey oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is tender and has large pores, it does not require oil to be applied, but rather should be washed after a rinse with rosewater, or cold water, or water from a morelle (a type of berry), or water from a cucumber, or porcelain water, or any other similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with excessive moisture should rise from it using myrrh water, and sumac, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excess fluid should rise from old wine, or eucalyptus water, or chamomile decoction, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to use a cupping glass before a bath or after a bath for one hour or two; and they should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he bathe when he needs cupping and after he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who have a hot temper and those who are too angry and inflamed; it is advisable for them to apply cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce, and similar things; and eat little, and porridge made from chaste tree fruit, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and moderate aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat many seeds and small birds; and on the day that he opens his pores, he must drink more than he eats; and it is necessary to give any man triacle or mace before or after opening the pores, to strengthen the main limbs; and let him be careful in doing so, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and podagra, and the belly and the bowels and the joints and the spine, for these parts cannot tolerate being struck, and they are only done so to draw blood from one part of the body to another, as we do with mammaries when nursing; to remove the viscosity from the member, as we apply suction cups to the belly and bowels to reduce a swelling; and to ease pain, when there is congestion or a stone, it may possibly draw out the congestion or abandon the stone in its place; and thus it acts when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these suction cups are empty to suck only; and they are never applied with too much heat, nor filled with cold water, as in cases of painful tears, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water, or water mixed with herbs suitable for that purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup (ventouse) administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have two parts in width, equal to half a palm, and on its edge around the middle there should be a small hole, as if one could push an needle through it, and it should be made of metal, soft enough not to hurt the patient when placed on the body; and there should be a crossbar of metal, either iron or steel, in the middle for gripping with a cloth, and they can vary in size, both large and small, according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the cups used on children are different from those used on adults, and the thin ones on the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.
