And one should place this suction cup over the member: take the wax cloth or linen, and place it through the suction cup along the stick that is inside the suction cup, so that the clear part of the suction cup does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we have mentioned, so that when you want to see if it goes in, it will go in, and remove the suction cup; and use the linen as before, and repeat often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of a suction cup used to treat pleurisy, or any acute condition, it has no stick or opening, and can only be applied when it is full of water, and placed on the member only briefly; its shape is as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without wounds that cannot be treated with cupping for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and in the case of naked parts like teeth or nails, and others like them; the quality of the wound is such that when you find veins that are clear and smooth without pus, take them; place them in a clear water bath until they become tender, and have nothing in their stomachs; then clean with vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the cups; and when they are hurt and complain, if there is a part where a cup can be applied, apply it, for this does much good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If that does not work, raise the limb from the bed and immerse it in water, repeatedly squeezing it; and if the swelling subsides too much after removing the cups, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and place it on top, until the swelling goes down; or sprinkle vitriol powder or alum, or similar things, as long as the swelling remains; or you can also use half-peeled fava beans, leaving them on the limb until they adhere to the swelling, which will drain it now; and if you need more, take other cups.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins refuse to be opened, so fiercely they are filled with blood, you should prick them with a fresh sharp needle until the vein bursts, and then cover them; and as soon as they feel the blood, they will contract; and when you see that they have contracted, sprinkle some aloes powder and fine silk on them, or ashes, and they will close now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book on fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the wise men of this treatise have observed things from this chapter that were never seen in any ancient books, nor read in letters; and for this reason the science is strange in our land, for I never found anyone good at it; and no one knows about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, on which I have studied so much that I have acquired the science, and by experience, and through the custom of my life; and here I have described to you what is contained in this chapter, and abridged it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is appropriate that we begin this book with a prologue that outlines the essence of the words and chapters where the wise men apply their understanding and focus on truth; so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, or torsion occurs in any part of the body, you must hasten to treat the patient on both sides, if nothing helps, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if it is too cold or too hot, and avoid cold foods like raw meat, cheese, and ice, and do not let the patient drink wine or consume any fatty foods. Do not overfill the body with meats that fill the veins, until you are certain there is no high abscess or spread of material in the limb; then return the patient to their previous state as they had before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be given foods that do not cause excessive flatulence, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and peas, and veal, and offal, and ox, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because part of the wound's healing causes movement, and more often the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken from old age or decrepitude cannot be well healed or fused according to their nature because of the stiffness of the members, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but take no heed, rather pull the broken bone with strong hands that join the member together, as it was before, and do not remove it entirely from its place, and for this reason, it is necessary to nourish with rich meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture is of two kinds, one from the upper part, and another from the lower part, and in this chapter I will tell you all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There is also a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, such as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, then it is a fracture with a very small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own way and proper instrument for restoration, according to the memory of the place; and the fracture of the bone is known because the joint is twisted, and it opens well from outside, and sounds under pressure from the hand; and when there is no twisting or splitting or small fracture, there is no fracture; but it can certainly have a twist or split or slight fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not need to move it with your hand, but apply medications that will follow, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes up in the air, and the two separated parts, it is necessary to put them now equally, so that abscesses form from there; and if hot abscesses come, let them remain for a while, until the abscesses calm down; then place it equally as much as you can gently and carefully, and know that the restoration of what is broken is lighter than the restorations of what is shattered; then hold it, as is necessary afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into pieces, and it is dislocated from two parts, whether it be with the hand or foot, or one of the small members, or at two joints, or at a joint and your hand; place the member according to its natural position, so that when the fragments of the broken member are in their proper places, rearrange them using all possible means, and take care not to cause the patient any further injury or pain through your actions, and adjust the two parts of the bone to their best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if it feels right in the hand, then you know it is not correctly aligned: dress it neatly, do not tighten it too much, nor press upon it as those who, through their actions, cause abscesses and contractions in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is completely stiff, be very gentle with the patient so that he does not move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor in turning, or in any other way; and take care that the limb is well secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet completely healed, and it is important to put him in a position where he feels no pain; and be careful that he is placed correctly, so that no deformity occurs as he recovers; and the quality of the damaged limb depends on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the damaged limb can be different in size and shape, and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Because it has small members, as arms and legs and similar: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen; and those that are large, like the thigh and leg: they should be wrapped in a wide and firm ligature, for the wide ligatures embrace the entire member, and tighten it equally from all sides so that there is no movement; then apply light bandages, three or four turns depending on the member, and tighten your hand slightly across the entire ligature; then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture can move a little; and soften the ligature little by little, until you press greatly upon the healthy part below; then take another ligature and wrap it around again from the beginning on the broken bone; then return to the part below the fracture, and tighten it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place between the firm linen bandages or strips of cloth until it is all even, then bind everything with a bandage above, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, apply a hot compress to the affected area, which reduces the swelling, and leave it for several days; then strain your eyes, and make them half the width of a large coin sharp, or from wood used to make chisels, or from palm leaves, following this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread placed on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and as long as required for the member, whether small or large; then strain the eyes as you did in the first layer, and tie them with a thread to hold, as in the first layer on the fracture; tighter now, looser later; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and of soft flax; for if the thread is thick, as I have often seen the fools who make their bindings from twisted flaxen threads, this is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it is not appropriate that there be less space between each eye.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is angry because of the pain from the stars after dislocating their joints, he should place them in a hot compress of lint or other soft cloth so that they do not get infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by fracture, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all the broken stars on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it is not appropriate to put stars inside for more than 5 or 7 days, or according to your judgment of the hot sore coming; and here you see the ancient method of pastes to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, make this preparation, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it; this is the common way of the paste that restores fractures in many ways, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to prepare a restorative plaster for fractures, dislocations, and twists: take arnica, ladanum, nettle, and camphor, each in equal parts; add myrrh and aloe, each in five parts; almonds, nine parts; and make it into powder, mixing it with egg white. If the patient's body heat is high, use this plaster, as it is of good composition and restores broken bones effectively, benefitting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for twists: take mugwort and chamomile, each in ten parts; myrrh and aloe, each in seven parts; akamide (a type of herb) six parts; Armenian bole (a mineral) ten parts; grind them well and mix with vinegar or egg white, then administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of splinting joints and realigning bones in their sockets, alleviating the pain that ensues, and using the bone for healing and mending: take a fresh cloth, soak it in hot water and oil, and place it over the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore proper function, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses and safely extracting bones that cause pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another splinting method that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pavot (opium poppy) leaves, crush them together, and make a paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of broken bones, and to alleviate the return of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the roots of broom, chamomile, violet flowers, and grain flour, in equal parts; grind them fine and mix with wine, applying this to the affected member. Alternatively, prepare it with fresh, moist coriander water or simple water, and apply as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering for the restoration of a stubborn, hard-to-heal abscess on the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vitex agnus-castus, flaxseed, alder, melilot, and fennel, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from each an equal part; grind them and conserve with vinegar, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the affected member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a broken member, one should use a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, stating it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen suggests that to restore a broken member, one should apply warm, dry substances such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is effective for pain and injury: take lint and feathers from chopped cloth or owl's pen feathers, and bark from a tree, all cut equally, and grind them into a paste and apply it and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after a little while, take care that the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place. If pain arises again, or itching, or swelling, then hasten to remove the plaster and take it off immediately; take a light cloth and a moist sponge, dip them in water, and lift up the limb until the itching stops and the pain is soothed. Then let the member rest for an hour, and apply a dry cloth moistened with water or rose oil, and wrap it tightly with a bandage, ensuring you are certain of the heat of the abscess; and thus the swelling of the limb will be relieved, and the pain gone, and then continue with the delicate process, applying a little more plaster, but not so tightly as before, and treat it gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red, swollen, painful, and filled with pus, and you need to apply a poultice and bind it, then repeat as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb does not heal after what we have said, do not release it until after three or four or five or seven days, and never leave it for twenty days while the fracture heals and the joint adjusts to its proper place; then tighten it more than before, and thicken the tissue as I mentioned previously. If you see that the limb is drying out more than necessary, know that healing will not occur. So apply hot water compresses every time you release it, once every third day, and gently massage the area; through this work, therefore, correct the limb's condition, and avert the harmful actions of the ignorant physician, who, by their actions, cause further damage: this is evil, and such practices should be avoided, and instead, follow them correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many methods of fracture, with various shapes and distinct causes; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the bone splits completely through, as if cut with a axe or a staff; and due to this, this type of fracture is called "haichure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without piercing it, and this method of fracture is called "absolute"; and these two types of fractures can be either large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a throbbing, or swelling, or cuts from stone chippings, or blows against stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which approaches the skin just beneath or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound which is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, this is called a "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by a stone, or a blow, or something similar, and the piece of bone enters below, and the bone ends are bent like the tongs when they grasp a cauldron, then between the stone and the bone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in those with moist heads of bones, such as the head of an infant; and it happens in all these ways of dislocation that small fragments are torn off, just as if they were broken. And I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of dislocations caused by traction on them, and the inquiry at close range, and by the corrupt flesh above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is noted because when the bone is discovered and rubbed gently, it opens the dislocation, revealing the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be wary of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any ill omens, such as vomiting, loss of senses, stiffness, paleness, ague fever, or other symptoms appearing in various combinations, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents and hope for a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the swelling comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the flesh under the bone is corrupted, then the complications arise that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone breaks down to the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part in this way: and you press the patient's head with pain, and uncover the bone in all ways possible, and clean the wound more gently than you can, and if the discharge of blood appears when uncovering the bone, or abscess at the base, you should seek help as appropriate, and fill the wound with moistened oil-soaked cloth; and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and be assured of the bleeding's cessation. Then, begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you make a narrow cut before, and this is its shape...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another treatment even greater than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is that you have many different-sized instruments, some with pointed and others with broad ends, all made of indurate iron, and use them gently so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is necessary that you pierce it from around, using instruments with edges, not making them go through the bone too deeply, so that the tip does not go beyond the other side; and you need several of them, so that each one goes in its proper place according to the density of the bone, allowing for precise cuts on all sides; and this is the form of the three types of instruments:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to know when an bone is broken is that you place pressure on the bone and return to your normal movement until you are sure the bone is pierced; then place pressure elsewhere a little later, and so continue all around, then cut with incisions the space between the breaks in the bone, and do this as delicately as possible, gently, while still holding the bone in your hand or with any of your tools like tweezers or pliers, and be careful not to touch the brain or the soft tissue.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary to observe the resistance that remains from the bone to any other tool resembling an incision knife, but it should be more gentle and delicate than the others; and if it does not hold onto the small bones or scales, gently remove them with the appropriate tools; then dress the wound with bandages and remedies as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer; it binds very tightly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either where the fracture is open, and when you have exposed this part, place the tip of this curved scalpel beneath it, whose shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but expose the acute part on the second side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike slightly with a small hammer, gently compressing the bone all around, and be very careful of the skin that is beneath; if it is detached from the bone, gently pull it, as it is easily removed without pain or harm.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is cut only from above, leaving small fragments, it is necessary to remove these rough edges with a fine rasper in sufficient quantity to make each part as suitable as possible, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great raspers (tools) and then more subtle ones, never stop doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to adjust according to their location; and this is something that is not fully answered to one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if it pleases him to reveal himself, you should press the bandage of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another bandage doubled over twice or three times, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first bandage; do this as lightly as possible so as not to weigh down the dressing, then apply another covering, but don't tighten it too much until the swelling has subsided; leave it like that for a day or two until the abscess is calmed, then remove it and apply medications such as lily roots, flour of times (spices), incense powder, arisology (herbal preparations), and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and administer foreign remedies without cauterization; ensure that the wound is always clean, so do not leave any dressing or allow it to form a lump, for when lumps gather in the flesh of the head, they will corrode and burst, and cause great harm to the patient, as when you place something sharp on the syph (fleshy bump) it becomes numb.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is questionable without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes not from the medicine that has been applied, and its virtue is in doubt, it is necessary to press a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and wrap it in a cloth, and place it on the affected area; then cure it with the remedies that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that the two parts of the bone are never broken, either together or separately, for they are two bones; and the cartilage in the middle is not broken, but only flexes or twists, then it becomes healed.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your little finger or a narrow tool between the bones, and put the fracture back in place with your index finger and thumb, until the bone returns to its natural position; do this gently, and be careful not to cause pain to the patient through your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the bone near the joint, and the bones cannot return to their original position, it is necessary that you place a slightly thicker rule across the top, so that the bones align correctly.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, repeat the same process, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if possible; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, once the abscess has subsided, then place thin linen strips over the fracture, if it is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you turn to another side, if it is broken; and make the bandages so thick that they fill the openings of the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required if the bandages are soaked in butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good, but it is necessary that they be soaked in a mixture of egg and flour powder; then leave the bandage, until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never should one apply the feathers of a goose directly to any part of the body without first testing them, and if they cause suffering around it, hold the break still, and let the patient breathe; or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear at the wound while you are treating it, apply a poultice or moist cotton in olive oil or in a small container of eagle's blood.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess forms, apply a poultice made of flour, incense powder, mixed with egg albumen, then place light bands on it and do not tie the wound; and if the break in the wound is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then clean the wound with hot things and treat it with ointments and bandages appropriate to it; and if there is no wound inside the neis, treat it lightly and apply plasters until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly displaced, and it is not broken into two pieces, but only out of place, then if you gently know how to handle it, it can be reset.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger of the left hand into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, press the fracture gently from inside with your right index finger, then use your other hand to pull it slightly outward, making them equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is severe in two parts, you must administer an extension to both parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, by stretching with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken mandible wax, and put a double cloth; and on the cloth, a large, well-made star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and fasten it to the muscles that you can, and command the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, on the third day, then reset it as it was; and apply plaster, mixing fine powder with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after removing the wax; and apply a thin layer of plaster, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, it is necessary to do as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, no part of the bone that is broken should be removed; it is necessary to carefully extract the suitable instruments from within.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have removed all these pieces and it does not delay, immediately close the wound if it is wide, and place suitable bands on it to prevent infection, until it heals.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three manners: it may be broken and detached in two parts, with fragments, and is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the work when the fracture is without an injury, you need two assistants: one should hold the aid that is broken, and the other stretch the collar towards the affected part; then put the fracture back into place with equal force, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no deformity or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch it further, place a round spear of cloth, or wool, under the patient's shoulder, as thick as necessary; extend and gently tighten the bandage, holding the spear with your hand, so that you make an even break, as is fitting.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the bandage away from the wound because it is stuck, then it is necessary that the patient lies on his side, and places a medium pillow under his shoulder, and asks his attendants to lift the bandage towards the back, until the bone in the bandage is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel any debris, it is necessary that you cut through; and pull out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined together by any means, take hold of one of the incisions you have made; but place the forcele (instrument) under the bone to protect it.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It resembles a spoon, and is not too sharp, and as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; it has two edges, as you can see, one broad, and the other thin, corresponding to the rupture of the wound you made when handling the bones; and when you are certain of the hot abscess, if the wound is deep, then use the wound of drapelets and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms, take a cloth dipped in rose oil, or aloe, or wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The straining of the bone, when it is wounded and broken, is that you apply a poultice of fine-milled powdery alum and egg white to the bone, and place light bandages over it, and put a spear under the joint, if necessary; then take a very wide strip of cloth, about a palm in width, and lay it double over the bandages and poultice; next, take a thin, pointed reed three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the cloth, so that the end of the cloth hangs down from the edge of the bandage; place the reed on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the healthy joint and the damaged one, and then tie it tightly under the armpit, and release the spear; repeat this process for each part, and when you see that the bandage holds firmly, and clearly see that the reed does not move over the broken bone, every day, and as the wound heals, and replace the bandage, if necessary. The bone should be healed in about 28 days, or less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated, do not attempt to reduce it by force or movement; instead, align it according to its natural shape and in every way possible. Then apply a fine, powdered mixture with enough egg, gently press it, and place a double cloth over it. Put a broad and thin steel plate, slightly wider than the shoulder, and secure it firmly with a great strap so that the plate does not move from its place; check it each day. Whenever it loosens, tighten the strap and ensure the plate remains in position. Place the patient on his side, and after approximately 20 days or a week (the exact number is unimportant), gently release it and be certain, for it is not a bone that returns easily to its place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out and is not removed from the inside, it pierces and causes inflammation in the abscess, so do as we have said to soothe the heat of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the fracture do worse
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The limb is never broken in the middle, but that happens rarely; it often breaks at the extreme.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines to the inside, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no improvement, and sometimes blood oozes out, and it opens up the openings in the broken bone, and everything feels good.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and puts a cushion between his shoulders, then presses them, and aligns the ribs with both hands, subtly making it even in all ways so that the bone figure is as it should be; then apply poultices and compresses over the subtle salt or other light bandage, wrap it in a cloth, secure it to the broken bone so that it does not move, and return the skin tautly to the back, tighten it skillfully, and check the healing every hour, and if it softens, tighten it; if it needs to be released due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, act quickly, release it, remove the poultice, and address what has come of cure in a manner. Then apply the poultice again and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the breakage of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the breakage of ribs occurs only in humans with large backs, and at the top inside, and they can only bend because they are clear; and anyone can feel it well through inquiry.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a board, if you have such a need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, as if from weeping, because the bone pierces the flesh; and it causes weakness in the arms, and sometimes fainting, with a great flow of blood, and it is a cause of much suffering and illness, and ancient physicians have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is of those who say that it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to push out the fracture inward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not pretend that abscesses will not form if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of you should place cups on the body to draw out blood, as this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cup might suck up excess blood due to the weakness of the constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say none of you should cover the wound with moist wool and oil, and put tents between the ribs to equalize the space around it, then be cured of pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear through the bone where the break occurred, and there is doubt in the mind of the patient, then it is necessary to make an incision into the broken ribcage, and place an instrument to hold it stable; and then one must cut the bone, gently pull, and then sew together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and dress it with bandages, until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, place moist, oil-soaked cloths over them and on the affected area; treat while the abscess is present, keeping the patient lying on their side where it is painful, until they heal.
de la brisure dou col	Of the dislocation of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No dislocation occurs in the collarbone bone, and rarely does it happen if it rains; also to the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to a person, and you want to know if they will recover, be wary if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and unable to move or stretch them, and if you pierce them with an needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is deadly in many ways, if they are silent and feel well when you squeeze them and they do not hurt, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and the patient will be cured if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things occur in the back of the spine, and you need to know if it is healthy or not, be careful if the joints are weakened, and if there are accidents that cause pain, and strong excretion and defecation without will; and when it is recalled to its belly, it causes strong excretion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is recalled to its back and wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing that it is deadly, do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to pass, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply hot poultices or oil of roses or oil of larkspur to the abscess, until it is soothed; then place a comforting and drying plaster on it, secure it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is out of place, it should be covered with a bandage; then the bone is set, and the two edges of the wound are sewn together, if it is large, with stitches, and dressed with healing ointment, until it is healed; and if the bone fragment, called the "fragment of the cow," is in your hand, you should place it back into its proper position with your left hand, then apply the bandage and splint on top, as needed; then tighten it, and if there are any bones out of place, reduce them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the fracture of the bone of the spine.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone of the spine is fractured, it usually occurs without much initial reduction at the site; and it lengthens, curves, and causes pain, stiffness, and swelling at the broken place for the patient.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the fracture; and you should know what the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then make an equal and natural-shaped fracture.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it inclines inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture appears.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have made it even, place a splint over it, then apply a piece of wood or iron, and hold the fracture still so that it does not move; and use the hand under the ribs until the bone is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, as long as the abscess remains calm, follow what we have said before; then return to restoration, holding it as appropriate, unless there is some adverse event; this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The "ajutoire" refers to the joint between the shoulder blade and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored using one of two methods: one involves taking a strong, thick piece of wood, roughly shaped as follows:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And hold the two feet together, and bend them upward, and place the patient in a sitting position; then stretch one broken arm over the leg until it becomes relaxed, and place a bandage of cloth around it, then rest on any heavy object or have someone lower it gently; then take both hands and align the break as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that we place the patient on his back and tie his hands to his neck, then instruct those assisting to apply pressure over the break in each hand, and extend them all equally.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too violent, hold the broken part firmly in place, and on the break, stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the top of the shoulder, you should place a medium tie beneath the acromion and another towards the throat, beneath the break; and if the break is on the side of the throat, you should put a light tie without strain, as long as the break remains even on the bone, then set it correctly and tighten it, taking care not to cause any new problems.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess appears, do not extract it for seven days; place a moist cloth dipped in rose oil on the abscess until it is calmed; then extract it, and the manner of extraction is to apply a splint to the fracture, then bring the arm up to the shoulder or chest, and put a bandage over the joint, and tighten it over the limb, so that the arm is raised straight, unless something prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use a wider and stronger splint than others, and leave two spaces between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the fracture by three times on each side; then tighten the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about the fracture, more strongly and less apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars and the straining, as we have said, when you restore the broken member, and you doubt the heat of the abscess, leave it bound for seven days, as we have said; then every three days check the binding, that no swelling or pain comes to the place, or the healing cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is appropriate, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not remove the binding for three days or more, and have the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place a soft cushion under the dislocated limb, equal in thickness, and every hour of the day and night, watch that the figure of the dislocated limb does not move or the bindings become slack. If it is suitable by the virtue of medicine, and he is given food as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is first subtilized; and when he begins to regain strength, it will be considerable.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the aid and leg should be reestablished after forty days; and then one must release and administer baths and medicinal ointments for the joint to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and painful, it may take up to ten days or two months to release it.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "fostile," of which one is small and supports the wrist, and the other is large, located below the small bone towards the hand; sometimes only the large bone breaks, or only the small one, or both may be fractured together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.
