When the small bones are broken, healing is quick and easy, but when the large ones are broken, recovery is difficult, and the pain is greater than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then a little gentle stretching and positioning them equally is sufficient.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then they should be pulled stronger; extend them on a pillow, with the palm of the hand higher than the other, and the small bones lower, crossing the patient over himself, with the pillow in front higher than the patient's hand, so that the patient feels no pain. Then have another assistant stretch their arm to the opposite side of the patient's hand, or to the joint, and another assistant on top.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set it even with the eyes, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if, in the fracture, each piece is set in its place, and if there is none that holds the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place by doing as we have said before, then it must be cut off and the bone healed.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if, with the fracture, there is an open wound, I have spoken of it in detail; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if, in the beginning of restoration, abscesses occur, then I apply a wrap made of oil and beeswax, neither too hard nor too soft, and bind it delicately until the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the plaster, and apply the pouder from fine grain with plenty of egg, then place the needles, and let the needle of the break be stronger than others, a little wider as well; know that it must have six or more needles in different positions: whether the break is in one bone or two; tighten over the break more than elsewhere, but less far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and make the drapes covering the break soft and moist, and not too hard nor too rough; and let the thread used to tie it be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if no adverse event comes to the member, such as itching that arises in the member, then it is necessary that you raise the member with hot water, until the itching is soothed; and allow the member not to be tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the stretching, and if the ligaments loosen and the bones deviate, or similar things, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then you should soften it slightly, and leave it for a few days until the swelling goes down, and then stretch it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said help the patient, then he should be loose for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If uncertain, then bind his hands to his chest, ensuring his collarbones are even, and guard against movement and digitation, and have him sleep on his back. Know that this fracture is restored in 30 days or 45 days, or perhaps in 20 days, according to the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and at the joints there are often small fractures, and it brings only pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to cut across the bone, and hold it straight in front of him equally; then he places his hand on a flat surface, and extends the damaged bones, making them even, as much as possible, and applies a splint while they heal; and puts an ointment and bandages, if there is no abscess, and then wraps it with a cloth according to the size.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is near the stomach of the plant, make a ball of cloth and instruct the patient to press it against their bruised limb; then pull with a long cloth, making the heart-shaped wound as large as the plant on the hand, and compress it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the open air, it is necessary that you place a stick above and another below on the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly all around the hand, and seal the gap between them.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in either of the fingers, make it even, as necessary; pull it with the plant, and if you see that a small stick straightened the fracture, and it does not move, do so. And if the fracture is in another finger, like the index or any other, make it even and bind it with the healthy finger afterward; or tie them all together, which is better, or place a stick as before; be careful in the restoration and arrangement of the abscess above, and support what comes, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hipbone
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The hipbone is often broken, and one can clearly see it when it returns to its position in front and behind; its restoration is done by binding it tightly over the break, and another from below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each limb equally to its side; this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hipbone, one of the ligaments should be bound towards the knee, and others should be bound below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then the ligaments of the knee should be loosened, and the extension should be downward; then put the splint across the bone with both hands, as much as its natural shape allows, and apply the plaster, and bind, so that no deformity occurs.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, leave it to soothe, then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in the same way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is advisable to wrap the fracture with a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, and remove the excess, then turn the leg until the heel reaches the root of the toe, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end up over the top; then turn back to the leg and thigh, and wrap the bandage, then place a pad on it, and put a star on the bone of the leg; then use the eighth part of soft cloth between the leg and thigh, to equalize the tension, then begin tying three or four turns around the fracture, and as you go higher, loosen it; then take the two threads you have passed between the leg and thigh, and tie three stars on top, then return to the bottom with the thread, until you reach below the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, so that no abscess or swelling occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, and the dislocation occurs, and you address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that are caught, if possible, one should do so; and if they cannot be removed, one should break the joint and pull it out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never should the foot be broken in this way when placing staples, as is done with the aid of a leg or an arm; nevertheless, the restoration done in such a manner does not benefit the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the foot is restored in 7 days, or fewer or more, according to the diversity of dispositions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the alley of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or an opening, it affects every wound, and feels painful, and everyone feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put equal parts together as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and place a round bandage if necessary, and tighten it appropriately, then follow all the arrangements that we have mentioned for other breaks, such as an abscess high up or anything similar; apply to each case what is appropriate, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "tibial" and the other "fibula"; and every fracture in the leg occurs as it does in the arm, and the treatment is the same for both, with all the necessary work. And if both bones are broken together, the leg can move in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bones are broken, they bend forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it clearly, and it bends inward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply the extension, and set it level, and tie the stars equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary that the fracture be ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter; and adjust according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that cover the leg from one side and from the other, long enough to reach from the knee to the foot; then wrap two bandages around it, tightening them in the middle, so that the leg cannot move to the right or left, and thus is well. And no one should administer any medicine along the length of the leg, but if it is made of cloth, they put the leg in a position to prevent movement, and properly apply this to the fracture where there is an abscess or other complication; and each day move the leg to see if there is any abscess or other accident; cure it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the toes can be dislocated, and there is no cure except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the bones in the foot are fractured and you see them stacked on top of each other, the patient feels great pain in their foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, then immediately place your foot on theirs, raising the bones, and press gently until they return to their proper place; then apply a splint and bandages above and below the affected area, placing a small, flat table under the foot, securing it properly, and wrapping it with drapes and other necessary items.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if he loosens the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if none of the bones are broken, but they are discolored, then restore them as we have said regarding the bones of the hand; then place a stick along the length of the bone, and make it slightly wider, and put the cloth under the foot as I have said, securing it tightly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then place on each bone a stick according to its quantity, wrapped in a strip of linen, and secure the cloth under the foot away from the stomach; so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, when we have spoken; and aid each case as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	On the fracture of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's bone in her hand is fractured and the swelling subsides, then incline her body forward from the waist, holding her from behind. Next, fill the cavity of the fracture with cotton and put on a poultice as thick as possible. Then lift the woman's back up and down gently until the cotton reaches the entrance to the fracture and returns the bone to its place. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton and when she has urinated, replace it, doing this for seven or eight days. If you see improvement, take a bladder of goat's hair and tie one end to the gap and blow through the other end until the bladder is inflated inside. The nature will heal the fracture; then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it heals completely.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said regarding the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from one who puts his study and skill into it, and heeds this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means various dispositions for the right way of restoration: understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When a stick is broken, take a goose throat and insert it into the stick; then wrap cloth around it and leave it for three days or longer, and it will heal naturally.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is important for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the leg or shoulder or similar, to be healed immediately, so that the healing which we have mentioned serves as testimony.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still a fracture from poison, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or on the same day, before abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess increases, leave the healing until it is completely healed, as long as the abscess is calm, and do not touch it for at least a day or two, otherwise you would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible through the opened heart, it is necessary that you place it gently with your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not appear to be even with your hands, then take this instrument which is of iron, having seven or eight inches in length, and the width should be according to the size of the wound; and for this purpose, it is best to press it three or four times, depending on what is required for each break; and it should be round and slightly thicker, so that it does not bend under pressure on the member at your command, and wider in front, thickening towards the middle in advance, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", therefore the dislocated bone should be placed back on the visible head of the bone; and hold it in place once, until it returns to its original position, and is even on both sides.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must hold the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, with a suitable instrument such as a chisel or saw, within your power, then remove what is remaining in the bone from sharpness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do your best to put it back in its place, then moisten the drape with black, sticky wine, and arrange it properly; do not put any ointment or oil on the wound, otherwise it may lead to putrefaction and corruption. Then administer stars (possibly a type of medicine) when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it around accordingly to its size, taking good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and often, the foolish do this and bring upon the patient either death or severe corrosion sometimes. And the bindings should be softer and more gentle than others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or great, and you doubt that some ill accident may come of it, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, if it does not need to be bound up; but wrap around, instead of bandages, strong cloth, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to close, then remove whatever you have placed over it, and apply healing ointment to the wound, such as a four-ingredient ointment and similar remedies.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it remains swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be dislocated in such a way that the bowstring moves gently downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for a long time, and it cannot heal but keeps returning to the bowed state, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, then you must clean the wound thoroughly and remove all these misplaced fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula occurs in the place or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and opened up in a limb, such as the bone of the shin or the shoulder, or other similar bones of large limbs, do not pull it, because many times death results from it, but let it heal on its own for twenty or thirty days; then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burn injuries that come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often encounter after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a terrible sight to see the misalignment of the limb; and in some cases, it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if we must treat it: If we administer astringent medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you press any of these things or all together, and conserve them with astringent wine or with abundance of heat or with cold, and place them on the wound firmly, and do not loosen them for many days; and then dislocate it and begin another, until the swelling is gone; or tighten it with a well-made pad, for the property of the pad lies in removing all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already become hard like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the excess, and cure it as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the weak and delicate member remains, this can happen for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not properly aligned; or because there are too many ligaments, preventing the normal movement of the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or from too much sudden movement, not in its natural time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and tighten the body, until the blood flow increases within it; then administer a bath, give joy and comfort, then apply lead to the member, so that the lead attracts great blood flow, and often moisten it with warm water, until the circulation reaches the limb, and it returns to its natural state.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Both members twisted after the dislocation.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the members are twisted after reduction and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish ones who say one must break the limb right away, and many foolish practices have been done in our land; and these practices are to be blamed, and great harm comes from them, and perhaps even death. However, if the contusions and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be treated with hot water or soft herbs cooked, like fennel leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things; and apply a mollifying plaster, as well as a good-made aqua vitae, and take the mucilage of fennel and confit it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply it as a plaster. Or you can use fig fats, crushed with colon powder and similar medicines that soften the stiffness.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the dislocation be subjected to continuous and prolonged friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the affected limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the swelling and stiffness are like stone, and require a sharp tool to release, one must carefully cut just below the bone, using a delicate saw; and apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations result from a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs due to no apparent reason, it is necessary to attempt to bring the limb back to its normal position immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limb swells, and by chance if it is reset at a later time, it becomes painful; therefore, it is not advisable to move it at that moment when it is swollen. This often causes inflammation and other pains; however, once the swelling has subsided, treat the patient, then soak the affected area in hot water and oil, gently reset the dislocated joint, and apply the appropriate cure as if it were in its normal position.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the upper limbs from the wrist to the shoulder.
des mandibules	and of the jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is often the case that the jaws become dislocated, and this dislocation occurs in two ways: either they are slightly out of their sockets, still somewhat flexible; or they are entirely dislocated, hanging down towards the chin, preventing the patient from closing their mouth, swallowing, or speaking, and their tongue moves with them.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must then reset it forcefully, without delay; and in such a way that the healer places the patient's head firmly with his sick hand, pressing it towards the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, where the dislocation is from two parts; and with the other two hands he pulls away equally. And command the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he adjusts the mirrors equally until they return to their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back (to the correct position), especially when both mandibles are involved, using hot water and oil, gently bringing them together; do not delay in resetting it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without straining, place moist cloth bandages made of rose oil and wax on it, then gently tie them with soft bindings; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their legs between two pillows so that they do not move to either side, nor make any effort to open their mouth more, until the pain is gone and the mandibles are healed. Then they can slowly eat and drink, avoiding opening their mouth widely while eating or drinking until the mandible is fully recovered.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly aligned within an hour and do not return to their normal position, then fever and persistent aches may occur, along with abdominal pain, or vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know it is a sign of impending death; and often those who experience it die within seven days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot dislocate from either side in the continuity of it, and from the worst side, it is never healed properly outside, and it causes great pain.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the joint at the base of the palm, and it returns; then he applies the plaster and bandage, and tightens it; and the dislocation which is by the side of the shoulder cannot move; if not, and if it moves even once, he must be put back in place, as we have said; then he applies the plaster and bandage, and tightens it, and instructs the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the same happens with the dislocation of the spine when it is out of its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	**Shoulder Dislocation**
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one when it dislocates at the acromion end; the second at the part of the scapula closest to the spine; and sometimes at the top, which happens rarely, and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder or inside for the nerves. It often dislocates outward towards the acromion, especially in those with little fat, because for them it goes severely; in those with enough fat, it barely moves and returns barely.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one that they feel a sharp pain or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary for you to test it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocations are recognized when they move towards the joint, and make a distinction between the injured shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their differences manifest; and you will find in the shoulder a hollow place, and by touching the shoulder blade, the top of the shoulder, as if it were one; and the patient cannot bring his arm to his body, nor move it in any way; and also, if it is dislocated high up, unless it is hidden, because you can feel it clearly by touching; and this kind of dislocation is not only for resetting when it is new or if there is an infection.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healer places his hand on top of the patient's pain, then places his palms underneath the joint, and pulls the joint upward with force; and the healer lifts his hand, extends it upward, and places it underneath; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as we have said, in a few days later, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and administer gently softening and soothing remedies such as a decoction of althae and fennel and melilote in water, and care for them; then support the patient's back, and place under the joint a piece of equal wool, neither too soft nor too hard, and place their heel on it, and gently lift the top of the shoulder, pulling the hand of the patient with it; and another assistant should hold the patient's head, so that it does not move. The shoulder will return immediately, as you can see, following this method: and make sure to have someone present who is stronger than the patient; and stand straight against the patient's side, take the shoulder away from under the joint of the affected arm, lift the joint upward, and pull the hand downward towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so that anything heavy causes him trouble, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also adjusted in another way: take a long stick and bury it in the ground so that its tip is as bright as a pistol, but not too thick or too thin; then place it under the patient, but with soft cloth on top, and the patient's arm should be stretched down on the other side, forming an angle; then the joint will return to its place. If for all the things we have said, this treatment does not work, then do as follows: take a stick from both arms, wide and long enough to enter completely under the joint, according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place a heavy cloth over the head, so that it does not hurt the patient, and put the patient on their side; then stretch out one arm above the head, and bind the aid to the head, and the arm to the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on the edge of a wide shovel, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now reset.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated in any way, it is necessary to put under the joint a thread of equal wool, then apply the plaster with a mixture of powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, over all the shoulder and around, then pull the joint back into place, and tie the bandage again on the plaster, and press the hand against the collarbone, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move slightly, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; then after a few days or seven, he moves it; and if it remains closed and is not softened, it heals.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is firmly stuck due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply cautery in three places, as it is described in the chapter of cautery or treatment.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if all this is done, and after seven days the joint loosens, and cannot raise its arm, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either compressed, stretched or damaged; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst, and the joints, or behind, if it is done by a blow, and stretching of the hands, and another cause, then it should be treated until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing, cracking occurs in the member, and delayed movement, if the patient uses it many times, until the cracking is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the dislocated joint is relieved at times, and then returns; if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not completely healed, for one can see and feel it well; and it heals according to its form.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated part with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, preventing the arm from bending or touching the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it in such a way that the abscess closes and doesn't reopen, for if it does reopen, resetting it will be difficult, especially when it's at the back; it is more painful than other dislocations and may even lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be brought back such that you extend his hand with both of yours; and his arms are spread out, and the hands are placed with care according to the cost around, from inside and outside, and bring the joint back to its place on his palms together, or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to its original position, and bring the base of the palm with the joint that is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer a strong extension; and have the second minister extend the arm, and gently pull it until it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side after you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint join with the hand, apply no oil to soften the joint, but tighten the joint firmly, until it returns; and once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, stretch the limb towards the patient's chest, and leave it for no more than a day, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for no days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels stiffness after the joint is reset, and it becomes mute, bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is relaxed; or apply a grease-soaked woolen compress to the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and immerse it in a bath; and when it has healed, rub the joint temperately, then apply the compress again, and repeat this process twice or three times until it is cured; and if you see that it remains stiff, use fine moist warm wax with butter, and strain it over the joint.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint is misaligned and its return to the original position is slight, more so than other joints. However, it must be carefully realigned while still in a dislocated state, so that the bones do not swell or an abscess forms near it.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the realignment is such that you place the patient's hand on a table, extend their fingers, and observe them until they are even, so that the palm is facing the dislocation, and hold it until it returns. However, you must carefully check if the joint is in its correct position; then place the patient's hand upside down on a table for extension and realignment.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on a table, and look to see where the joint appears.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good. Otherwise, if the strain of soothing emplasters does not cease, and he leaves it thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place for any number of days, then the joint remains twisted; and it causes no further harm to the patient as long as the hand is flexible, and nothing can be extracted: then know that a nerve or an artery is cut; and there is no other mechanism by which to extract it safely, and perhaps there is no other remedy.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is dislocated, if you place on it the splint that we have said, then pull and hold it for a day, then release it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is no fracture, then apply hot water moistened cloth and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the two joints of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The joints of the hand should never be dislocated at each side, nor at the back of the palm or on the palm itself; then pull and release the joint until it returns to its place, then support the two joints and bend the dislocated one towards the part where it is separated; leave it for a day, and then set it again as it was before; and do not bind it, but release it the next day, make it move, and reconnect it; and repeat this often until it tightens up, and do the same if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, following the same method until it heals; and also do the same when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the collarbone is dislocated and there is no cure, the patient's condition worsens rapidly and death may ensue.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs of this are that the patient's bowels move involuntarily, and they cannot control them, and often a limb becomes limp, either the two legs or both arms, or even both; sometimes the spine becomes curved in three parts; the part that curves backward is called 'scoliosis'. The cure for this, if it arises from childhood, is to strengthen the affected area; if there is no remedy or treatment at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, the old ways of treatment speak in great words, but they offer little benefit to all; but I have abbreviated it according to my intent and formed tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the foot first, no one has any knowledge of it; and also that which comes directly to one side, and it is only the one who properly comes to the back who can cure it, as I say; and it is that the patient should be stretched out on his face equally in the first position, and have traction from below so that he does not move; then insert a stick into the ground in a curved shape, and another at the foot, and tie a string around the afflicted parts, and another on the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and these minsters know the strings, one at the head and the others at the feet among the two sticks; and they should be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the skilled person places his palms on the curved spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board three feet long, cut a notch in the wall from the inside, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the board away from the wall; then place the middle of the board over the spine; and put both legs on the other side of the board, pressing firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do this with a twist that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two sticks, each as long as the arm of the patient, and insert them at the side, directing two others towards the feet; and between each stick, cut notches, deep and away from the body, about three fingers' breadth long; and each stick should have a hole through which it is firmly attached to the ground so that they do not move; and between these two sticks, there should be another turning stick, with two small sticks one finger's breadth long on either side, for the turn; and then tie the thong that connects the pegs to the turns towards the head, and the other thong towards the feet to the opposite turn; and each assistant twists their turn to its full length, and the master makes sure the spine is aligned as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, then the compresses, and then the end of a tablet three fingers long, which shall attach the joint to the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said before, and use the patient's gentle rest, until he is healed; and if any thing occurs at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, in the manner that we have mentioned above; and never apply a piece of cloth, nor let there be any appearance on the rear spine, and take care lest it be dislocation; and this is the bone which opens, for which reason one must not be presumptuous: perhaps death would result.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the spine and the joints of the shoulder only result in dislocations, unlike other joints; and the joint of the spine is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, less misaligned at the front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, the affected knee is more extended and opens wider than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee fully; it is the joint that is located next to the abscess, as the root of the thigh comes over.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who is about to die is that this event is contrary to what has happened before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of someone who is about to die include: their leg being strong according to its strength; however, do not bend the knee without pain, and if they want to walk, they cannot, and they hold their urine, and the angle of their limb swells, and when they look down, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of someone who is about to die from behind include: they cannot spread or bend their knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the angle of the limb becomes soft, and the foot is in a different position compared to the hip, towards the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They reset this appearance of dislocation if it is that you recognize the dislocation being old and it persists according to its nature, unless there is no cure; and he must not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one where the dislocation is recent, and it's of the four types of dislocation, you must act quickly, restoring the joint to its proper position within and outside, and ensuring it's aligned correctly to the right and left; if done properly, it may heal on its own and no other treatment is required.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it doesn't return in this manner, you must apply a strong force, extending the leg strongly with two hands, or binding it firmly to the knee; other ministers should place their hands above in such a way that they press the patient's hands against their sides, then pull strongly on the foot with a steady grip, located on the calf; others hold the head with the same firm grip; and all at once, pulling upwards and downwards, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, remaining still until healed.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four parts, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If it is not, it is necessary to take care of this aspect. When the dislocation is in the hip joint, it is important that you help the patient lie on their healthy side, then tie a bandage around the root of the thigh, and the joint that is above the angle. Then extend the bandage upwards towards the angle and downwards towards the strong point. Then have another assistant support the patient's arms, and hug the large joint of the injured thigh, extending it to the extreme limit; it will return to its place now, and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have said, then it is necessary that you tie both feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligature on both heels and knees, and let the leg of the patient be extended two handbreadths more than the other; then hang him by his head from a post, and let his body hang two arm-lengths above the ground; then command the minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and have other ministers hanging with the patient, who embrace the thigh, for the joint will now come back together.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is external, if the patient lies as we have said in the case of the dislocated joint, then carefully remove the ligature from the leg of the patient, also from the foot; then place two sticks, one at the head and another at the feet, and insert a stick between the cuisses of the patient, following their form; and wrap moist towels around them so that they do not hurt the patient, then stretch each minister towards him, and make them put their hands equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, put it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is present, it is necessary to extend the affected leg forcefully, as I have said; and to alleviate the patient's pain from being on the sore joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch it downwards towards the knee.
