Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the outside, it is not appropriate to stretch the affected leg downwards, nor lift it up onto the table, but rather it should remain in a position similar to how the hip was dislocated outwardly, as we have said gently on both hips; and place it on its face, and extend the leg as we have said above, and press on the joint against the table; and it will be at the point when the patient extends their legs, and they are even. Then tighten the socks, and apply a plaster, and a strap from a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then loosen it, and apply a plaster to it, and let the member heal gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The limb is dislocated in three ways: internally, externally, and backward; but not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if it does not return to its place at the knee, then know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend their leg if they can, and lay their face on your hand, and place their foot on yours. Then take hold of the knee in both hands, and pull between your fingers, and bend the two sides of the knee; and another assistant extends the patient's foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that the leg moves slightly at the knee; then apply a poultice, and straighten the leg with respect to the knee, and bind it together firmly for three or four days, and then loosen it; and do not let the patient move about, until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, apply firm extension as we have said in the treatment of the neck, as long as it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is neither completely dislocated nor fully healed, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tender in the area where it is dislocated; the reduction is slight, and one should gently extend their fingers towards the affected side when it is slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from all sides, you should make the patient lie straight, and hold the leg with both hands above the ankle; then take the foot in your right hand and pull it to you, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and turn the foot nicely up; and do this twice as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it comes back, that's good; if not, begin the treatment again, for it will come back; and if it cannot come back like that, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and insert a firm peg between his thighs, and wrap blankets around him so he does not hurt himself; then have the assistants hold the thigh, and others stretch the foot to its joints, or tie it to the ankle of the healthy leg; then each assistant stretches it equally, and the peg should be in place between the patient's thighs to hold him when they stretch him; then put your hands on either side of the dislocation, and another assistant turns the healthy leg over, and the dislocation will return steadily.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when the wound is at its deepest, apply a poultice and compress it, forming a strain around it, and fasten the foot to the leg, securing the stirrups behind the ankle so that the ligaments do not become too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the strain lessens, loosen it on the third day or fourth. Then remove it after four days, and have the patient walk for three days; and if this does not end well, it is not certain that he will heal further.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, it is necessary to soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, while it remains healthy.
des dois	Of the two (parts/sides).
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two (parts/sides) are disaligned, if they need to be properly aligned without strain, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the back or leg, it is necessary that you place the patient on a flat or straight table and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with your foot's form until it returns; and when it is even and there is nothing open, place a wooden block under the sole of the foot, then stretch it strongly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	from wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you wish to restore it, often the patient dies if you are not cautious in treatment: so be not presumptuous in attending to it, unless you are skilled in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and be neither hasty nor hard-hearted; and at first use hot applications on the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of recovery; but when there is hope, reset the limb gently, so that the abscess does not return; and when the limb is in place again, apply hot applications to the abscess and treat the wound as appropriate from desiccation; and if there is a fracture or small broken bones, set them as we have said for simple ailments; and beware of entering a path of fear, as I have mentioned, for it is up to you to move according to your Creator, and because of your knowledge of arming and caring for your body.
